data-file-height=\"59\"></div>\r\n<div style=\"position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 59px; width: 100px; height: 36px; background-color: #;\"><img style=\"vertical-align: top;\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/12/Kit_shorts_lalakers_statement.png\" alt=\"Kit shorts lalakers statement.png\" width=\"100\" height=\"36\" data-file-width=\"100\" data-file-height=\"36\"></div>\r\n<div style=\"position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 59px; width: 100px; height: 36px;\"><img style=\"vertical-align: top;\" title=\"Team colours\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kit_shorts.svg/100px-Kit_shorts.svg.png\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kit_shorts.svg/150px-Kit_shorts.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kit_shorts.svg/200px-Kit_shorts.svg.png 2x\" alt=\"Team colours\" width=\"100\" height=\"36\" data-file-width=\"100\" data-file-height=\"36\"></div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div style=\"padding-top: 0.6em; text-align: center;\"><strong>Statement</strong></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</td>\r\n</tr>\r\n<tr>\r\n<td>\r\n<div style=\"width: 100px; margin: 0 auto; padding: 0;\">\r\n<div style=\"background-color: white; position: relative; left: 0px; top: 0px; width: 100px; height: 95px; margin: 0 auto; padding: 0;\">\r\n<div style=\"position: absolute; left: 31px; top: 0px; width: 38px; height: 59px; background-color: #4c2b94;\"><img style=\"vertical-align: top;\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/be/Kit_body_lalakers_classic2223.png\" alt=\"Kit body lalakers classic2223.png\" width=\"38\" height=\"59\" data-file-width=\"38\" data-file-height=\"59\"></div>\r\n<div style=\"position: absolute; left: 31px; top: 0px; width: 38px; height: 59px;\"><img style=\"vertical-align: top;\" title=\"Classic jersey\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Kit_body_basketball.svg/38px-Kit_body_basketball.svg.png\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Kit_body_basketball.svg/57px-Kit_body_basketball.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Kit_body_basketball.svg/76px-Kit_body_basketball.svg.png 2x\" alt=\"Classic jersey\" width=\"38\" height=\"59\" data-file-width=\"38\" data-file-height=\"59\"></div>\r\n<div style=\"position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 59px; width: 100px; height: 36px; background-color: #4c2b94;\"><img style=\"vertical-align: top;\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/13/Kit_shorts_lalakers_classic2223.png\" alt=\"Kit shorts lalakers classic2223.png\" width=\"100\" height=\"36\" data-file-width=\"100\" data-file-height=\"36\"></div>\r\n<div style=\"position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 59px; width: 100px; height: 36px;\"><img style=\"vertical-align: top;\" title=\"Team colours\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kit_shorts.svg/100px-Kit_shorts.svg.png\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kit_shorts.svg/150px-Kit_shorts.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Kit_shorts.svg/200px-Kit_shorts.svg.png 2x\" alt=\"Team colours\" width=\"100\" height=\"36\" data-file-width=\"100\" data-file-height=\"36\"></div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div style=\"padding-top: 0.6em; text-align: center;\"><strong>Classic</strong></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</td>\r\n</tr>\r\n</tbody>\r\n</table>\r\n</td>\r\n</tr>\r\n</tbody>\r\n</table>\r\n<p>The <strong>Los Angeles Lakers</strong> are an American professional <a title=\"Basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basketball\">basketball</a> team based in <a title=\"Los Angeles\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles\">Los Angeles</a>. The Lakers compete in the <a title=\"National Basketball Association\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_Association\">National Basketball Association</a> (NBA) as a member of the league's <a title=\"Western Conference (NBA)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Conference_(NBA)\">Western Conference</a> <a title=\"Pacific Division (NBA)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_Division_(NBA)\">Pacific Division</a>. The Lakers play their home games at <a title=\"Crypto.com Arena\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crypto.com_Arena\">Crypto.com Arena</a>, an arena shared with the NBA's <a title=\"Los Angeles Clippers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Clippers\">Los Angeles Clippers</a>, the <a title=\"Los Angeles Sparks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Sparks\">Los Angeles Sparks</a> of the <a title=\"Women's National Basketball Association\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association\">Women's National Basketball Association</a>, and the <a title=\"Los Angeles Kings\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Kings\">Los Angeles Kings</a> of the <a title=\"National Hockey League\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Hockey_League\">National Hockey League</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-9\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-9\">[9]</a></sup> The Lakers are one of the most successful teams in the history of the NBA, and have won 17 NBA championships, tied with the <a title=\"Boston Celtics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics\">Boston Celtics</a> for the most in NBA history.<sup id=\"cite_ref-10\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-10\">[10]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The franchise began with the 1947 purchase of a disbanded team, the Detroit Gems of the <a title=\"National Basketball League (United States)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_League_(United_States)\">National Basketball League</a> (NBL). The new team began playing in <a title=\"Minneapolis\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minneapolis\">Minneapolis</a>, <a title=\"Minnesota\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minnesota\">Minnesota</a>, calling themselves the <strong>Minneapolis Lakers</strong>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-The_Nicknames_11-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-The_Nicknames-11\">[11]</a></sup> Initially a member of the NBL, the Lakers won the 1948 NBL championship before joining the rival <a title=\"Basketball Association of America\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basketball_Association_of_America\">Basketball Association of America</a>, where they would win five of the next six championships, led by star <a title=\"George Mikan\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Mikan\">George Mikan</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Mike_12-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Mike-12\">[12]</a></sup> After struggling financially in the late 1950s following Mikan's retirement, they <a title=\"Relocation of professional sports teams\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relocation_of_professional_sports_teams\">relocated</a> to Los Angeles before the <a title=\"1960&ndash;61 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1960%E2%80%9361_NBA_season\">1960&ndash;61 season</a>.</p>\r\n<p>Led by <a title=\"Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame\">Hall of Famers</a> <a title=\"Elgin Baylor\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elgin_Baylor\">Elgin Baylor</a> and <a title=\"Jerry West\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerry_West\">Jerry West</a>, Los Angeles made the <a title=\"NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a> six times in the 1960s, but lost every series to the Celtics, beginning their <a title=\"Celtics&ndash;Lakers rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celtics%E2%80%93Lakers_rivalry\">long and storied rivalry</a>. In 1968, the Lakers acquired four-time <a title=\"NBA Most Valuable Player Award\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Most_Valuable_Player_Award\">NBA Most Valuable Player</a> (MVP) <a title=\"Wilt Chamberlain\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilt_Chamberlain\">Wilt Chamberlain</a>, and won their sixth NBA title&mdash;and first in Los Angeles&mdash;in <a title=\"1971&ndash;72 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_NBA_season\">1972</a>, led by new head coach <a title=\"Bill Sharman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Sharman\">Bill Sharman</a>. After the retirement of West and Chamberlain, the team traded for superstar <a title=\"Kareem Abdul-Jabbar\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar\">Kareem Abdul-Jabbar</a>, who would win three MVP awards as a Laker. While the team was unable to advance to the Finals in the late 1970s, two momentous changes came in 1979 that would inaugurate a new golden era for the franchise. First, <a title=\"Jerry Buss\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerry_Buss\">Jerry Buss</a> purchased the Lakers, and as the team's owner, pioneered a vision of basketball games as entertainment spectacles as well as sporting events.<sup id=\"cite_ref-13\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-13\">[13]</a></sup> Second, the Lakers drafted <a title=\"Magic Johnson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magic_Johnson\">Magic Johnson</a> <a title=\"List of first overall NBA draft picks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_first_overall_NBA_draft_picks\">first overall</a> in the <a title=\"1979 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1979_NBA_draft\">1979 NBA draft</a>.</p>\r\n<p>The combination of Johnson, a passing prodigy <a title=\"Point guard\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Point_guard\">point guard</a>, and a dominant <a title=\"Center (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center_(basketball)\">center</a> in Abdul-Jabbar provided the Lakers with two superstars to anchor their roster. The promotion of head coach <a title=\"Pat Riley\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Riley\">Pat Riley</a> in 1981 and the addition of forward <a title=\"James Worthy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Worthy\">James Worthy</a> through the <a title=\"1982 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_NBA_draft\">1982 draft</a> established the Lakers as an NBA powerhouse throughout the 1980s. The team was nicknamed the \"<a title=\"Showtime (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Showtime_(basketball)\">Showtime Lakers</a>\" due to its fast break, transition offense facilitated by Johnson. The franchise won five championships in a nine-year span, including winning two out of three marquee Finals matchups against the Celtics. The Lakers were defeated by their Boston archrivals in the <a title=\"1984 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984_NBA_Finals\">1984 Finals</a>, but triumphed over the Celtics in <a title=\"1985 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1985_NBA_Finals\">1985</a> and <a title=\"1987 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1987_NBA_Finals\">1987</a>.</p>\r\n<p>After Riley departed and Abdul-Jabbar, Johnson, and Worthy all retired, the Lakers struggled in the early 1990s. It was not until 1996 when the team traded with the <a title=\"Charlotte Hornets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlotte_Hornets\">Charlotte Hornets</a> for the draft rights to <a title=\"Kobe Bryant\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kobe_Bryant\">Kobe Bryant</a> and signed star center <a title=\"Shaquille O'Neal\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaquille_O%27Neal\">Shaquille O'Neal</a> that the Lakers returned to dominance during the early 2000s. The superstar duo of Bryant and O'Neal, along with Hall of Fame coach <a title=\"Phil Jackson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phil_Jackson\">Phil Jackson</a>, led the Lakers to three consecutive championships between <a title=\"2000 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000_NBA_Finals\">2000</a> and <a title=\"2002 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_NBA_Finals\">2002</a>, securing the franchise's second \"<a title=\"Three-peat\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three-peat\">three-peat</a>.\"<sup id=\"cite_ref-14\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-14\">[14]</a></sup> The dynamic but tumultuous \"<a title=\"Shaq&ndash;Kobe feud\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaq%E2%80%93Kobe_feud\">Shaq-and-Kobe</a>\" era ended when the Lakers traded away O'Neal after the team lost to the <a title=\"Detroit Pistons\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Detroit_Pistons\">Detroit Pistons</a> in the <a title=\"2004 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_NBA_Finals\">2004 Finals</a>. It was not until after the Lakers traded for <a title=\"Pau Gasol\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pau_Gasol\">Pau Gasol</a> that Bryant and Jackson returned to the NBA Finals, losing to the Celtics in <a title=\"2008 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_NBA_Finals\">2008</a> but winning two more championships in <a title=\"2009 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_NBA_Finals\">2009</a> and <a title=\"2010 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_NBA_Finals\">2010</a>. The 2010 Finals marked the latest matchup of the Lakers and Celtics, with Los Angeles winning its 16th title against its ancient rival in a seven-game series.</p>\r\n<p>Jackson retired from coaching in 2011, and after a string of tumultuous playoff exits, the Lakers endured their longest playoff drought in franchise history. Gasol departed as a free agent in 2014, and Bryant retired in 2016 after twenty years as a Laker. After multiple rebuilding seasons with young, highly rated prospects, the Lakers signed superstar <a title=\"LeBron James\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LeBron_James\">LeBron James</a> in 2018.<sup id=\"cite_ref-15\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-15\">[15]</a></sup> In 2019, the team traded several of those prospects for star <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Big man (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_man_(basketball)\">big man</a> <a title=\"Anthony Davis\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthony_Davis\">Anthony Davis</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-16\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-16\">[16]</a></sup> The Lakers&mdash;led by James, Davis, and head coach <a title=\"Frank Vogel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Vogel\">Frank Vogel</a>&mdash;won the team's 17th championship in <a title=\"2020 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_NBA_Finals\">2020</a>, tying the Celtics for the most titles in NBA history.<sup id=\"cite_ref-17\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-17\">[17]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Lakers hold the record for <a title=\"List of National Basketball Association longest winning streaks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_National_Basketball_Association_longest_winning_streaks\">NBA's longest winning streak</a>, 33 straight games, set during the 1971&ndash;72 season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-18\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-18\">[18]</a></sup> Twenty-six Hall of Famers have played for Los Angeles, while four have coached the team. Four players&mdash;Abdul-Jabbar, Johnson, O'Neal, and Bryant&mdash;have won a combined eight NBA MVP awards with the Lakers.<sup id=\"cite_ref-19\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-19\">[19]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Franchise_history\" class=\"mw-headline\">Franchise history</span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"History of the Los Angeles Lakers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Los_Angeles_Lakers\">History of the Los Angeles Lakers</a></div>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1947.E2.80.931954:_Beginnings_and_Minneapolis_dynasty_with_George_Mikan\"></span><span id=\"1947&ndash;1954:_Beginnings_and_Minneapolis_dynasty_with_George_Mikan\" class=\"mw-headline\">1947&ndash;1954: Beginnings and Minneapolis dynasty with George Mikan</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Benjamin_Berger_speaking_at_the_National_Jewish_Fund_Dinner.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Benjamin_Berger_speaking_at_the_National_Jewish_Fund_Dinner.jpg/170px-Benjamin_Berger_speaking_at_the_National_Jewish_Fund_Dinner.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Benjamin_Berger_speaking_at_the_National_Jewish_Fund_Dinner.jpg/255px-Benjamin_Berger_speaking_at_the_National_Jewish_Fund_Dinner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Benjamin_Berger_speaking_at_the_National_Jewish_Fund_Dinner.jpg/340px-Benjamin_Berger_speaking_at_the_National_Jewish_Fund_Dinner.jpg 2x\" width=\"170\" height=\"181\" data-file-width=\"414\" data-file-height=\"442\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">Minneapolis team co-owner Benjamin Berger</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>The Lakers' franchise began in 1947 when <a title=\"Ben Berger\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Berger\">Ben Berger</a> and <a title=\"Morris Chalfen\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morris_Chalfen\">Morris Chalfen</a> of <a title=\"Minnesota\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minnesota\">Minnesota</a> purchased the recently disbanded Detroit Gems<sup id=\"cite_ref-20\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-20\">[20]</a></sup> of the <a title=\"National Basketball League (United States)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_League_(United_States)\">National Basketball League</a> (NBL) for $15,000 from Gems owner Maury Winston.<sup id=\"cite_ref-21\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-21\">[21]</a></sup> Minneapolis sportswriter <a title=\"Sid Hartman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sid_Hartman\">Sid Hartman</a> played a key behind-the-scenes role in helping put together the deal and later the team.<sup id=\"cite_ref-22\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-22\">[22]</a></sup> Inspired by Minnesota's nickname, \"Land of 10,000 Lakes\", the team christened themselves the Lakers.<sup id=\"cite_ref-The_Nicknames_11-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-The_Nicknames-11\">[11]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-23\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-23\">[23]</a></sup> Hartman helped them hire <a title=\"John Kundla\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Kundla\">John Kundla</a> from <a title=\"University of St. Thomas (Minnesota)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_St._Thomas_(Minnesota)\">College of St. Thomas</a>, to be their first head coach, by meeting with him and selling him on the team.<sup id=\"cite_ref-24\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-24\">[24]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-25\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-25\">[25]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Lakers had a solid roster, which featured forward <a title=\"Jim Pollard\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Pollard\">Jim Pollard</a>, playmaker <a title=\"Herm Schaefer\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herm_Schaefer\">Herm Schaefer</a>, and center <a title=\"George Mikan\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Mikan\">George Mikan</a>, who became the most dominant player in the NBL.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Minneapolis_Lakers_26-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Minneapolis_Lakers-26\">[26]</a></sup> In their first season, they led the league with a 43&ndash;17 record, later winning the NBL Championship that season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-27\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-27\">[27]</a></sup></p>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tleft\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:GeorgeMikan.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/GeorgeMikan.jpg/170px-GeorgeMikan.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/GeorgeMikan.jpg/255px-GeorgeMikan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/GeorgeMikan.jpg/340px-GeorgeMikan.jpg 2x\" width=\"170\" height=\"217\" data-file-width=\"2957\" data-file-height=\"3773\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tleft\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">Hall of Famer <a title=\"George Mikan\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Mikan\">George Mikan</a> (#99) led the Lakers franchise to their first five NBA championships. He is described by the NBA's official website as the \"first superstar\" in league history.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Mike_12-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Mike-12\">[12]</a></sup></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>In 1948, the Lakers moved from the NBL to the <a title=\"Basketball Association of America\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basketball_Association_of_America\">Basketball Association of America</a> (BAA), and Mikan's 28.3 point per game (ppg) scoring average set a BAA record. In the <a title=\"1949 BAA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949_BAA_Finals\">1949 BAA Finals</a> they won the championship, beating the <a title=\"Washington Capitols\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_Capitols\">Washington Capitols</a> four games to two.<sup id=\"cite_ref-28\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-28\">[28]</a></sup> The following season, the team improved to 51&ndash;17, repeating as champions.<sup id=\"cite_ref-29\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-29\">[29]</a></sup> In the 1950&ndash;51 season, Mikan won his third straight scoring title at 28.4&nbsp;ppg and the Lakers went 44&ndash;24 to win their second straight division title.<sup id=\"cite_ref-mikan_30-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-mikan-30\">[30]</a></sup> One of those games, a 19&ndash;18 loss against the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Fort Wayne Pistons\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fort_Wayne_Pistons\">Fort Wayne Pistons</a>, became infamous as the lowest scoring game in NBA history.<sup id=\"cite_ref-31\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-31\">[31]</a></sup> In the playoffs, they defeated the <a title=\"Indianapolis Olympians\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indianapolis_Olympians\">Indianapolis Olympians</a> in three games but lost to the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Rochester Royals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rochester_Royals\">Rochester Royals</a> in the next round.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Minneapolis_Lakers_26-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Minneapolis_Lakers-26\">[26]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>During the <a title=\"1951&ndash;52 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1951%E2%80%9352_NBA_season\">1951&ndash;52 season</a>, the Lakers won 40 games, finishing second in their division.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL_32-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL-32\">[32]</a></sup> They faced the <a title=\"New York Knicks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Knicks\">New York Knicks</a> in the <a title=\"1952 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1952_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a>, which they won in seven games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-La46_33-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-La46-33\">[33]</a></sup> In the <a title=\"1952&ndash;53 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1952%E2%80%9353_NBA_season\">1952&ndash;53</a> season, Mikan led the NBA in rebounding, averaging 14.4 rebounds per game (rpg), and was named MVP of the <a title=\"1953 NBA All-Star Game\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1953_NBA_All-Star_Game\">1953 NBA All-Star Game</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-mikan_30-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-mikan-30\">[30]</a></sup> After a 48&ndash;22 regular season, the Lakers defeated the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Fort Wayne Pistons\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fort_Wayne_Pistons\">Fort Wayne Pistons</a> in the Western playoffs to advance to <a title=\"1953 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1953_NBA_Finals\">the NBA Finals</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-La46_33-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-La46-33\">[33]</a></sup> They then defeated the New York Knicks to win their second straight championship.<sup id=\"cite_ref-La50_34-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-La50-34\">[34]</a></sup> Though Lakers star George Mikan suffered from knee problems throughout the <a title=\"1953&ndash;54 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1953%E2%80%9354_NBA_season\">1953&ndash;54</a> season, he was still able to average 18&nbsp;ppg.<sup id=\"cite_ref-La49_35-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-La49-35\">[35]</a></sup> <a title=\"Clyde Lovellette\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clyde_Lovellette\">Clyde Lovellette</a>, who was drafted in <a title=\"1952 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1952_NBA_draft\">1952</a>, helped the team win the Western Division.<sup id=\"cite_ref-La49_35-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-La49-35\">[35]</a></sup> The team won its third straight championship in the 1950s and fifth in six seasons when it defeated the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Syracuse Nationals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syracuse_Nationals\">Syracuse Nationals</a> in seven games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-La50_34-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-La50-34\">[34]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1954.E2.80.931958:_Post-Mikan_dry_spell\"></span><span id=\"1954&ndash;1958:_Post-Mikan_dry_spell\" class=\"mw-headline\">1954&ndash;1958: Post-Mikan dry spell</span></h3>\r\n<p>Following Mikan's retirement in the 1954 off-season, the Lakers struggled but still managed to win 40 games. Although they defeated the Rochester Royals in the first round of the playoffs, they were defeated by the Fort Wayne Pistons in the semifinals.<sup id=\"cite_ref-36\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-36\">[36]</a></sup> Although they had losing records the next two seasons, they made the playoffs each year.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL_32-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL-32\">[32]</a></sup> Mikan came back for the last half of the <a title=\"1955&ndash;56 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1955%E2%80%9356_NBA_season\">1955&ndash;56 season</a>, but struggled and retired for good after the season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-37\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-37\">[37]</a></sup> Led by Lovellette's 20.6 points and 13.5 rebounds, they advanced to the Conference Finals in 1956&ndash;57. The Lakers had one of the worst seasons in team history in 1957&ndash;58 when they won a league-low 19 games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-38\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-38\">[38]</a></sup> They had hired Mikan, who had been the team's general manager for the previous two seasons, as head coach to replace Kundla. Mikan was fired in January when the team was 9&ndash;30, and Kundla was rehired.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL_32-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL-32\">[32]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-39\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-39\">[39]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Lakers earned the top pick in the <a title=\"1958 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1958_NBA_draft\">1958 NBA draft</a> and used it to select <a title=\"Elgin Baylor\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elgin_Baylor\">Elgin Baylor</a>. Baylor, who was named <a title=\"NBA Rookie of the Year Award\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Rookie_of_the_Year_Award\">NBA Rookie of the Year</a> and co-MVP of the <a title=\"1959 NBA All-Star Game\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1959_NBA_All-Star_Game\">1959 NBA All-Star Game</a>, averaged 24.9&nbsp;ppg and 15.0&nbsp;rpg helping the Lakers improve to second in their division despite a 33&ndash;39 record.<sup id=\"cite_ref-40\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-40\">[40]</a></sup> After upsetting the Hawks in six games in the division finals, they returned to the NBA Finals, but were swept by the Celtics, beginning their long rivalry.<sup id=\"cite_ref-41\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-41\">[41]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1958.E2.80.931968:_Move_to_Los_Angeles_and_Celtics_rivalry\"></span><span id=\"1958&ndash;1968:_Move_to_Los_Angeles_and_Celtics_rivalry\" class=\"mw-headline\">1958&ndash;1968: Move to Los Angeles and Celtics rivalry</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Baylor,_Chambers_and_West.jpeg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Baylor%2C_Chambers_and_West.jpeg/170px-Baylor%2C_Chambers_and_West.jpeg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Baylor%2C_Chambers_and_West.jpeg/255px-Baylor%2C_Chambers_and_West.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Baylor%2C_Chambers_and_West.jpeg/340px-Baylor%2C_Chambers_and_West.jpeg 2x\" width=\"170\" height=\"192\" data-file-width=\"411\" data-file-height=\"465\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Elgin Baylor\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elgin_Baylor\">Elgin Baylor</a> (left) and <a title=\"Jerry West\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerry_West\">Jerry West</a> (right) led the team to a total of ten NBA Finals appearances in the 1960s and 1970s. Nicknamed \"Mr. Clutch\", West's silhouette is featured on the NBA's official logo.<sup id=\"cite_ref-42\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-42\">[42]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-43\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-43\">[43]</a></sup></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>In their <a title=\"1959&ndash;60 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1959%E2%80%9360_NBA_season\">last year</a> in Minneapolis, the Lakers went 25&ndash;50. On January 18, 1960, the team was coming off a loss and traveling to St. Louis when their plane crash-landed.<sup id=\"cite_ref-44\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-44\">[44]</a></sup> Snow storms had driven the pilot 150 miles off course when he was forced to land in a cornfield. No one was hurt.<sup id=\"cite_ref-45\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-45\">[45]</a></sup> Their record earned them the number two pick in the <a title=\"1960 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1960_NBA_draft\">1960 NBA draft</a>. The team selected <a title=\"Jerry West\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerry_West\">Jerry West</a> from <a title=\"West Virginia Mountaineers men's basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Virginia_Mountaineers_men%27s_basketball\">West Virginia University</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-46\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-46\">[46]</a></sup> During the 1960 off-season, the Lakers became the NBA's first West Coast team when owner <a title=\"Bob Short\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Short\">Bob Short</a> decided to move the team to Los Angeles.<sup id=\"cite_ref-History_of_the_Lakers_#_10_47-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-History_of_the_Lakers_#_10-47\">[47]</a></sup> Led by Baylor's 34.8&nbsp;ppg and 19.8&nbsp;rpg, Los Angeles won 11 more than the year before in West's first season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL1961_48-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL1961-48\">[48]</a></sup> On November 15 that season, Baylor set a new NBA scoring record when he scored 71 points in a victory against the New York Knicks while grabbing 25 rebounds.<sup id=\"cite_ref-49\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-49\">[49]</a></sup> In doing so, Baylor broke his own NBA record of 64 points. Despite a losing record, the Lakers made <a title=\"1961 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1961_NBA_playoffs\">the playoffs</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL_32-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL-32\">[32]</a></sup> They came within two points of the <a title=\"1961 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1961_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a> when they lost in game seven of their second round series against St. Louis.<sup id=\"cite_ref-50\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-50\">[50]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Led by Baylor and West at 38.3 and 30.8&nbsp;ppg respectively,<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL1962_51-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL1962-51\">[51]</a></sup> the Lakers improved to 54&ndash;26 in <a title=\"1961&ndash;62 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1961%E2%80%9362_NBA_season\">1961&ndash;62</a>, and made the <a title=\"1962 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1962_NBA_Finals\">finals</a>. In a game five victory, Baylor grabbed 22 rebounds and set the still-standing NBA record for points in a finals game with 61,<sup id=\"cite_ref-52\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-52\">[52]</a></sup> despite fouling out of the game.<sup id=\"cite_ref-53\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-53\">[53]</a></sup> The Lakers, however, lost to the Celtics by three points in overtime of game seven.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL1962_51-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL1962-51\">[51]</a></sup> <a title=\"Frank Selvy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Selvy\">Frank Selvy</a>, after making two jumpers in the final 40 seconds to tie the game,<sup id=\"cite_ref-54\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-54\">[54]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-Selvy_55-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Selvy-55\">[55]</a></sup> missed a potential game-winning 18&nbsp;foot <a title=\"Jump shot (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jump_shot_(basketball)\">jump shot</a> in regulation, a miss which he said in June 2010 still haunted him more than 40 years later.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Selvy_55-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Selvy-55\">[55]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Los Angeles won 53 games in <a title=\"1962&ndash;63 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1962%E2%80%9363_NBA_season\">1962&ndash;63</a>, behind Baylor's 34.0&nbsp;ppg and West's 27.1&nbsp;ppg<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL1963_56-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL1963-56\">[56]</a></sup> but lost in the NBA Finals in six games to the Celtics.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL1963_56-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL1963-56\">[56]</a></sup> After falling to 42&ndash;38 and losing in the first round of the <a title=\"1964 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1964_NBA_playoffs\">1964 NBA playoffs</a> to the Hawks, the team won 49 games in 1964&ndash;65. The Lakers surged past the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Baltimore Bullets (1963&ndash;73)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baltimore_Bullets_(1963%E2%80%9373)\">Baltimore Bullets</a> in the division finals, behind West's record-setting 46.3&nbsp;ppg in the series.<sup id=\"cite_ref-57\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-57\">[57]</a></sup> They lost again to Celtics in the Finals however, this time in five games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-58\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-58\">[58]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Los Angeles lost in the finals to Boston in seven games again in 1966, this time by two points.<sup id=\"cite_ref-59\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-59\">[59]</a></sup> Down by 16 entering the fourth quarter, and 10 with a minute and a half to go, the Lakers mounted a furious rally in the closing moments, which fell just short.<sup id=\"cite_ref-60\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-60\">[60]</a></sup> After dropping to 36 wins and losing in the first round of the <a title=\"1967 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1967_NBA_playoffs\">1967 NBA playoffs</a>, they lost in the finals to the Celtics again <a title=\"1968 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1968_NBA_Finals\">in 1968</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL_32-4\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL-32\">[32]</a></sup> Los Angeles moved to a brand-new arena, <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"The Forum (Inglewood, California)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Forum_(Inglewood,_California)\">The Forum</a>, in 1967, after playing seven seasons at the <a title=\"Los Angeles Memorial Sports Arena\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Memorial_Sports_Arena\">Los Angeles Memorial Sports Arena</a>.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1968.E2.80.931973:_The_arrival_of_Wilt_Chamberlain\"></span><span id=\"1968&ndash;1973:_The_arrival_of_Wilt_Chamberlain\" class=\"mw-headline\">1968&ndash;1973: The arrival of Wilt Chamberlain</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wilt_Chamberlain_1972.jpeg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Wilt_Chamberlain_1972.jpeg/170px-Wilt_Chamberlain_1972.jpeg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Wilt_Chamberlain_1972.jpeg/255px-Wilt_Chamberlain_1972.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Wilt_Chamberlain_1972.jpeg/340px-Wilt_Chamberlain_1972.jpeg 2x\" width=\"170\" height=\"282\" data-file-width=\"513\" data-file-height=\"852\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Wilt Chamberlain\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilt_Chamberlain\">Wilt Chamberlain</a> played for Los Angeles for five seasons during the late 1960s and early 1970s. He was an integral part of their <a title=\"1971&ndash;72 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1971&ndash;72 team</a> that is considered one of the best in NBA history.<sup id=\"cite_ref-nba10_61-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-nba10-61\">[61]</a></sup></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>On July 9, 1968, the team acquired <a title=\"Wilt Chamberlain\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilt_Chamberlain\">Wilt Chamberlain</a> from the <a title=\"Philadelphia 76ers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philadelphia_76ers\">Philadelphia 76ers</a> for Darrell Imhoff, <a title=\"Archie Clark (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archie_Clark_(basketball)\">Archie Clark</a>, and <a title=\"Jerry Chambers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerry_Chambers\">Jerry Chambers</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-62\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-62\">[62]</a></sup> In his first season as a Laker, Chamberlain set a team record by averaging a league-leading 21.1&nbsp;rpg.<sup id=\"cite_ref-chamberlain_63-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-chamberlain-63\">[63]</a></sup> West, Baylor, and Chamberlain each averaged over 20 points, and Los Angeles won their division.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL1969_64-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL1969-64\">[64]</a></sup> The Lakers and Celtics again met in the <a title=\"1969 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1969_NBA_Finals\">finals</a>, and Los Angeles had home court advantage against Boston for the first time in their rivalry. They won the first game behind Jerry West's 53 points,<sup id=\"cite_ref-65\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-65\">[65]</a></sup> and had a 3&ndash;2 lead after five.<sup id=\"cite_ref-66\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-66\">[66]</a></sup> Boston won the series in seven games however,<sup id=\"cite_ref-67\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-67\">[67]</a></sup> and earned their 11th NBA Championship in 13 seasons.<sup id=\"cite_ref-68\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-68\">[68]</a></sup> West was named the first-ever <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"NBA Finals MVP Award\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Finals_MVP_Award\">Finals MVP</a>; this remains the only time that a member of the losing team has won the award.<sup id=\"cite_ref-69\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-69\">[69]</a></sup> In <a title=\"1969&ndash;70 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1969%E2%80%9370_NBA_season\">1970</a>, West won his first scoring title at 31.2&nbsp;ppg, the team returned to the <a title=\"1970 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970_NBA_Finals\">finals</a>, and for the first time in 16 years, they did not have to face the Celtics; instead playing the New York Knicks, who defeated them 4&ndash;3.<sup id=\"cite_ref-NBA_Finals:_All-Time_Champions_70-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-NBA_Finals:_All-Time_Champions-70\">[70]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-1970_NBA_Finals_71-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-1970_NBA_Finals-71\">[71]</a></sup> The <a title=\"1970&ndash;71 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970%E2%80%9371_NBA_season\">next season</a> the Lakers were defeated by the <a title=\"Milwaukee Bucks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milwaukee_Bucks\">Milwaukee Bucks</a>, led by future Laker Lew Alcindor (now known as <a title=\"Kareem Abdul-Jabbar\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar\">Kareem Abdul-Jabbar</a>) in the Western Conference Finals.<sup id=\"cite_ref-72\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-72\">[72]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The <a title=\"1971&ndash;72 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_NBA_season\">1971&ndash;72 season</a> brought several changes. Owner <a title=\"Jack Kent Cooke\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jack_Kent_Cooke\">Jack Kent Cooke</a> brought in <a title=\"Bill Sharman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Sharman\">Bill Sharman</a> as head coach,<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#15_73-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#15-73\">[73]</a></sup> and Elgin Baylor announced his retirement early in the season after realizing that his legs were not healthy enough.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#15_73-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#15-73\">[73]</a></sup> Sharman increased the team's discipline.<sup id=\"cite_ref-74\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-74\">[74]</a></sup> He introduced the concept of the <a title=\"Shootaround\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shootaround\">shootaround</a>, where players would arrive at the arena early in the morning before a game to practice shots.<sup id=\"cite_ref-75\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-75\">[75]</a></sup> They won 14 straight games in November and all 16 games played in December.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#15_73-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#15-73\">[73]</a></sup> They won three straight to open the year of 1972 but on January 9, the Milwaukee Bucks ended their winning streak by defeating the Lakers, 120&ndash;104.<sup id=\"cite_ref-76\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-76\">[76]</a></sup> By winning 33 straight games, Los Angeles set a record for longest winning streak of any team in major American professional team sports.<sup id=\"cite_ref-77\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-77\">[77]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-78\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-78\">[78]</a></sup> The Lakers won 69 games that season, which stood as the NBA record for 24 years until the Chicago Bulls won 72 games in 1995&ndash;96.<sup id=\"cite_ref-79\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-79\">[79]</a></sup> Chamberlain averaged a low 14.8 points but led the league in rebounding at 19.2 a game.<sup id=\"cite_ref-ballref72_80-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-ballref72-80\">[80]</a></sup> West's 9.7 assists per game (apg) led the league, he also averaged more than 25 points, and was named MVP of the <a title=\"1972 NBA All-Star Game\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_NBA_All-Star_Game\">1972 NBA All-Star Game</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-ballref72_80-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-ballref72-80\">[80]</a></sup> The team failed to score 100 points just once all year,<sup id=\"cite_ref-81\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-81\">[81]</a></sup> and at the end of the season, Bill Sharman was named <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"NBA Coach of the Year\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Coach_of_the_Year\">Coach of the Year</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-82\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-82\">[82]</a></sup> The Lakers went on to reach the <a title=\"1972 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972_NBA_Finals\">finals</a> against the <a title=\"New York Knicks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Knicks\">New York Knicks</a> where they would avenge their 1970 <a title=\"1970 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970_NBA_Finals\">finals</a> loss by defeating them 4 games to 1. Chamberlain tallied 24 points and 29 rebounds in game five and won the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Bill Russell NBA Finals Most Valuable Player Award\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Russell_NBA_Finals_Most_Valuable_Player_Award\">NBA Finals Most Valuable Player Award</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-83\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-83\">[83]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-84\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-84\">[84]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Lakers won 60 games in the <a title=\"1972&ndash;73 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972%E2%80%9373_NBA_season\">1972&ndash;73 season</a>, and took another Pacific Division title.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_History_#16_85-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_History_#16-85\">[85]</a></sup> Wilt Chamberlain, playing in his final season, again led the league in rebounding and set the still standing NBA record for field-goal percentage at 72.7%.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_History_#16_85-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_History_#16-85\">[85]</a></sup> The team defeated the Chicago Bulls in seven games in the conference semifinals, then the <a title=\"Golden State Warriors\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors\">Golden State Warriors</a> in five in the Western Division Finals.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_History_#16_85-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_History_#16-85\">[85]</a></sup> They played the New York Knicks in the <a title=\"1973 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_NBA_Finals\">1973 NBA Finals</a>. Los Angeles took the first game by three points, but New York won the series in five games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-86\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-86\">[86]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1973.E2.80.931979:_Building_.22Showtime.22\"></span><span id=\"1973&ndash;1979:_Building_&quot;Showtime&quot;\" class=\"mw-headline\">1973&ndash;1979: Building \"Showtime\"</span></h3>\r\n<p>During the <a title=\"1973&ndash;74 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973%E2%80%9374_NBA_season\">1973&ndash;74 season</a>, the team was hampered by the loss of West, who played only 31 games before his legs gave out.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#16_87-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#16-87\">[87]</a></sup> Goodrich, averaging 25.3 points, helped the team to a late-season surge.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#16_87-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#16-87\">[87]</a></sup> Trailing the Golden State Warriors by three games with seven left to play, the Lakers rallied to finish 47&ndash;35 and win the Pacific Division.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#16_87-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#16-87\">[87]</a></sup> They made the playoffs but managed just one win against Milwaukee in the conference semifinals. Following the season, West retired due to contract disagreements with Cooke, and filed a suit for unpaid back wages.<sup id=\"cite_ref-88\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-88\">[88]</a></sup></p>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tleft\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar_1975.jpeg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar_1975.jpeg/170px-Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar_1975.jpeg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar_1975.jpeg/255px-Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar_1975.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar_1975.jpeg/340px-Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar_1975.jpeg 2x\" width=\"170\" height=\"228\" data-file-width=\"1352\" data-file-height=\"1812\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tleft\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">The Lakers acquired <a title=\"Kareem Abdul-Jabbar\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar\">Kareem Abdul-Jabbar</a> in 1975.</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>After missing the playoffs in the <a title=\"1974&ndash;75 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1974%E2%80%9375_NBA_season\">1974&ndash;75 season</a>, the Lakers acquired <a title=\"Kareem Abdul-Jabbar\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kareem_Abdul-Jabbar\">Kareem Abdul-Jabbar</a>, who had won three league MVPs by that time.<sup id=\"cite_ref-89\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-89\">[89]</a></sup> Abdul-Jabbar wanted out of Milwaukee, demanding a trade to either New York or Los Angeles.<sup id=\"cite_ref-90\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-90\">[90]</a></sup> He was traded for <a title=\"Elmore Smith\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elmore_Smith\">Elmore Smith</a>, <a title=\"Brian Winters\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Winters\">Brian Winters</a>, <a title=\"Junior Bridgeman\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Junior_Bridgeman\">Junior Bridgeman</a>, and <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"David Meyers (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Meyers_(basketball)\">Dave Meyers</a>. Abdul-Jabbar had his fourth MVP season in <a title=\"1975&ndash;76 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1975%E2%80%9376_NBA_season\">1975&ndash;76</a>, leading the league in rebounding, blocked shots, and minutes played.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#17_91-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#17-91\">[91]</a></sup> The Lakers struggled in January, going 3&ndash;10, and finished out of the playoffs at 40&ndash;42.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#17_91-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#17-91\">[91]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>West and Cooke settled their differences&mdash;and the former Laker's lawsuit&mdash;and Cooke hired him to replace Sharman as the team's coach.<sup id=\"cite_ref-92\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-92\">[92]</a></sup> West became upset, however, when Cooke refused to spend the money necessary to acquire forward <a title=\"Julius Erving\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julius_Erving\">Julius Erving</a>, who the Nets were selling.<sup id=\"cite_ref-93\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-93\">[93]</a></sup> Behind another MVP season from Abdul-Jabbar, Los Angeles won the Pacific Division, finishing the 1976&ndash;77 season a league-best 53&ndash;29.<sup id=\"cite_ref-94\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-94\">[94]</a></sup> They defeated the Warriors in a seven-game series to open the postseason before being swept by Portland in the Western Conference Finals.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#17_91-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#17-91\">[91]</a></sup> During the off-season, Los Angeles picked up <a title=\"Jamaal Wilkes\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jamaal_Wilkes\">Jamaal Wilkes</a> from Golden State and signed first-round draft pick <a title=\"Norm Nixon\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norm_Nixon\">Norm Nixon</a>.</p>\r\n<p>In the first two minutes of the first game of the 1977&ndash;78 season, Abdul-Jabbar punched Bucks center <a title=\"Kent Benson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kent_Benson\">Kent Benson</a> for an overly aggressive elbow and broke his hand.<sup id=\"cite_ref-95\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-95\">[95]</a></sup> Two months later, a healthy Abdul-Jabbar got into an altercation with <a title=\"Houston Rockets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houston_Rockets\">Houston Rockets</a> center <a title=\"Kevin Kunnert\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_Kunnert\">Kevin Kunnert</a> after a rebound. The team's starting power forward, <a title=\"Kermit Washington\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kermit_Washington\">Kermit Washington</a>, who was averaging 11.5 points and 11.2 rebounds,<sup id=\"cite_ref-96\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-96\">[96]</a></sup> entered the fight, and when <a title=\"Rudy Tomjanovich\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rudy_Tomjanovich\">Rudy Tomjanovich</a> ran in from the bench to break up the action, Washington punched him in the face.<sup id=\"cite_ref-97\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-97\">[97]</a></sup> Tomjanovich nearly died from the punch, suffering a fractured skull and other facial injuries, which prematurely ended his playing career.<sup id=\"cite_ref-98\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-98\">[98]</a></sup> Washington, who stated that he assumed Tomjanovich was a combatant, was suspended for two months by the NBA, and released by the Lakers.<sup id=\"cite_ref-99\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-99\">[99]</a></sup> The team won 45 games despite being down a starter in Washington and not having Abdul-Jabbar for nearly two months, but lost in the first round of the playoffs to Seattle.<sup id=\"cite_ref-100\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-100\">[100]</a></sup> During the 1978&ndash;79 season, the team posted a 47&ndash;35 record but lost to the SuperSonics in the semifinal round of the playoffs.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#17_91-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#17-91\">[91]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1979.E2.80.931991:_.22Showtime.22\"></span><span id=\"1979&ndash;1991:_&quot;Showtime&quot;\" class=\"mw-headline\">1979&ndash;1991: \"Showtime\"</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Further information: <a title=\"Showtime (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Showtime_(basketball)\">Showtime (basketball)</a></div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Magic_Lipofsky.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Magic_Lipofsky.jpg/170px-Magic_Lipofsky.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7d/Magic_Lipofsky.jpg 1.5x\" width=\"170\" height=\"180\" data-file-width=\"236\" data-file-height=\"250\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Magic Johnson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magic_Johnson\">Magic Johnson</a> along with Kareem Abdul-Jabbar led the \"Showtime\" Lakers to five NBA titles in the 1980s.</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>In the <a title=\"1979 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1979_NBA_draft\">1979 NBA draft</a>, Los Angeles selected <span class=\"nowrap\">6-foot, 9-inch</span> <a title=\"Point guard\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Point_guard\">point guard</a> <a title=\"Magic Johnson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magic_Johnson\">Magic Johnson</a> from <a title=\"Michigan State Spartans men's basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans_men%27s_basketball\">Michigan State</a> with the first overall pick.<sup id=\"cite_ref-101\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-101\">[101]</a></sup> It took Johnson's teammates time to acclimate themselves to his passing ability, as his \"no-look\" passes often caught them unaware. Once they adjusted, his passing became a key part of Los Angeles' offense.<sup id=\"cite_ref-102\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-102\">[102]</a></sup> The Lakers won 60 games in Johnson's rookie year, and defeated the <a title=\"1979&ndash;80 Philadelphia 76ers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1979%E2%80%9380_Philadelphia_76ers_season\">Philadelphia 76ers</a> in six games in the <a title=\"1980 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980_NBA_Finals\">1980 NBA Finals</a>. Johnson won the Finals MVP award, after starting at center for the injured Abdul-Jabbar in game six, and tallying 42 points, 15 rebounds, and seven assists.<sup id=\"cite_ref-103\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-103\">[103]</a></sup> The team fell off in the <a title=\"1980&ndash;81 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1980&ndash;81 season</a>, though, as the Lakers lost Johnson for most of the season to a knee injury.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#19_104-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#19-104\">[104]</a></sup> The team turned in a 54&ndash;28 record and finished second behind the <a title=\"1980&ndash;81 Phoenix Suns season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_Phoenix_Suns_season\">Phoenix Suns</a> in the Pacific Division.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#19_104-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#19-104\">[104]</a></sup> The <a title=\"1980&ndash;81 Houston Rockets season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_Houston_Rockets_season\">Rockets</a>, led by <a title=\"Moses Malone\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moses_Malone\">Moses Malone</a>, defeated Los Angeles in the first round of the playoffs.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#19_104-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#19-104\">[104]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Early in the <a title=\"1981&ndash;82 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1981&ndash;82 season</a>, Johnson complained to the media about head coach <a title=\"Paul Westhead\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Westhead\">Paul Westhead</a> and demanded a trade.<sup id=\"cite_ref-105\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-105\">[105]</a></sup> Westhead was fired shortly after Johnson's criticisms, and although Lakers' owner <a title=\"Jerry Buss\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerry_Buss\">Jerry Buss</a> stated that Johnson's comments did not factor into the decision, Johnson was vilified by the national media and booed both on the road and at home.<sup id=\"cite_ref-106\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-106\">[106]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-107\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-107\">[107]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-108\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-108\">[108]</a></sup> Buss promoted assistant coach <a title=\"Pat Riley\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Riley\">Pat Riley</a> to \"co-head coach\" with Jerry West (although West considered himself Riley's assistant) on November 19 and the team won 17 of its next 20 games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#19_104-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#19-104\">[104]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-Buss_109-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Buss-109\">[109]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-110\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-110\">[110]</a></sup> Nicknamed \"<a title=\"Showtime (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Showtime_(basketball)\">Showtime</a>\" due to the team's new Johnson-led fast break-offense, the Lakers won the Pacific Division title and swept both the <a title=\"1981&ndash;82 Phoenix Suns season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_Phoenix_Suns_season\">Suns</a> and <a title=\"1981&ndash;82 San Antonio Spurs season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_San_Antonio_Spurs_season\">Spurs</a> in the <a title=\"1982 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_NBA_playoffs\">1982 playoffs</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-111\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-111\">[111]</a></sup> Los Angeles stretched its postseason winning streak to nine games by taking the first contest of the <a title=\"1982 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a> from the <a title=\"1981&ndash;82 Philadelphia 76ers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1981%E2%80%9382_Philadelphia_76ers_season\">76ers</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#19_104-4\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#19-104\">[104]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-112\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-112\">[112]</a></sup> The team won the Finals 4&ndash;2 to finish a 12&ndash;2 playoff run.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#19_104-5\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#19-104\">[104]</a></sup> On draft night in <a title=\"1982 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_NBA_draft\">1982</a>, the Lakers had the first overall pick (the result of a trade with Cleveland midway through the 1979&ndash;80 season, when the Lakers had sent Don Ford and a 1980 first-round pick to the Cavaliers for Butch Lee and their 1982 selection) and selected <a title=\"James Worthy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Worthy\">James Worthy</a> from <a title=\"North Carolina Tar Heels men's basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_basketball\">North Carolina</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-A_Worthy_Draft_Pick_113-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-A_Worthy_Draft_Pick-113\">[113]</a></sup> The <a title=\"1982&ndash;83 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">Lakers</a> won the Pacific Division at 58&ndash;24, but Worthy suffered a leg injury in the last week of the season and missed the rest of the season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-La222_114-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-La222-114\">[114]</a></sup> Nevertheless, they advanced to play <a title=\"1982&ndash;83 Philadelphia 76ers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_Philadelphia_76ers_season\">Philadelphia</a> in the <a title=\"1983 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1983_NBA_Finals\">1983 NBA Finals</a> after defeating <a title=\"1982&ndash;83 Portland Trail Blazers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_Portland_Trail_Blazers_season\">Portland</a> and <a title=\"1982&ndash;83 San Antonio Spurs season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982%E2%80%9383_San_Antonio_Spurs_season\">San Antonio</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-La222_114-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-La222-114\">[114]</a></sup> The Sixers, however, won the series and the championship in four games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-A_Worthy_Draft_Pick_113-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-A_Worthy_Draft_Pick-113\">[113]</a></sup> After the season West replaced Sharman as the team's GM.<sup id=\"cite_ref-115\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-115\">[115]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In the <a title=\"1983&ndash;84 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1983%E2%80%9384_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1983&ndash;84 season</a>, Los Angeles went 54&ndash;28, and played <a title=\"1983&ndash;84 Boston Celtics season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1983%E2%80%9384_Boston_Celtics_season\">Boston</a> in the <a title=\"1984 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984_NBA_Finals\">Finals</a> for the first time since <a title=\"1969 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1969_NBA_Finals\">1969</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-NBAF_116-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-NBAF-116\">[116]</a></sup> The Lakers won two of the first three games. However, <a title=\"Kevin McHale (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kevin_McHale_(basketball)\">Kevin McHale</a>'s hard <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Clothesline from hell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clothesline_from_hell\">clothesline</a> foul of Lakers forward <a title=\"Kurt Rambis\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurt_Rambis\">Kurt Rambis</a> on a fast break is credited as a turning point of the series.<sup id=\"cite_ref-117\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-117\">[117]</a></sup> Boston won three of the next four to win the title and send Los Angeles's record to 0&ndash;8 in Finals series against the Celtics.<sup id=\"cite_ref-NBAF_116-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-NBAF-116\">[116]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Using the past year's Finals defeat as motivation, <a title=\"1984&ndash;85 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">the team</a> won the Pacific Division for the fourth straight year and lost just two games in the <a title=\"1985 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1985_NBA_playoffs\">Western Conference playoffs</a>. In the <a title=\"1985 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1985_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a>, the <a title=\"1984&ndash;85 Boston Celtics season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_Boston_Celtics_season\">Celtics</a> were again the Lakers' final hurdle. Los Angeles lost game one of the NBA Finals by a score of 148&ndash;114, in what is remembered as the \"Memorial Day Massacre\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-Kareem,_Lakers_Conquer_the_Celtic_Mystique_118-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Kareem,_Lakers_Conquer_the_Celtic_Mystique-118\">[118]</a></sup> The Lakers, behind 38-year-old Finals MVP Abdul-Jabbar, recovered to defeat the Celtics in six games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-119\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-119\">[119]</a></sup> The team won the title in the <a title=\"Boston Garden\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Garden\">Boston Garden</a>, becoming the only visiting team to ever win an NBA championship there.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Kareem,_Lakers_Conquer_the_Celtic_Mystique_118-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Kareem,_Lakers_Conquer_the_Celtic_Mystique-118\">[118]</a></sup></p>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:James_Worthy_at_UNC_Basketball_game._February_10,_2007.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/James_Worthy_at_UNC_Basketball_game._February_10%2C_2007.jpg/170px-James_Worthy_at_UNC_Basketball_game._February_10%2C_2007.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/James_Worthy_at_UNC_Basketball_game._February_10%2C_2007.jpg/255px-James_Worthy_at_UNC_Basketball_game._February_10%2C_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/James_Worthy_at_UNC_Basketball_game._February_10%2C_2007.jpg/340px-James_Worthy_at_UNC_Basketball_game._February_10%2C_2007.jpg 2x\" width=\"170\" height=\"260\" data-file-width=\"558\" data-file-height=\"854\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">Los Angeles drafted <a title=\"James Worthy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Worthy\">James Worthy</a> first overall in 1982. \"Big Game James\" recorded his only career <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Triple double\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triple_double\">triple double</a> in the Lakers game seven victory over the Pistons in the 1988 NBA Finals.<sup id=\"cite_ref-120\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-120\">[120]</a></sup></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>In the <a title=\"1985&ndash;86 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1985&ndash;86 season</a>, the Lakers started 24&ndash;3 and went on to win 62 games and their fifth straight division title.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_games_in_the_1985&ndash;1986_NBA_season_and_playoffs_121-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_games_in_the_1985&ndash;1986_NBA_season_and_playoffs-121\">[121]</a></sup> The <a title=\"1985&ndash;86 Houston Rockets season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_Houston_Rockets_season\">Rockets</a>, however, defeated the Lakers in five games in the <a title=\"1986 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986_NBA_playoffs\">Western Conference Finals</a>. Houston won the series when <a title=\"Ralph Sampson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ralph_Sampson\">Ralph Sampson</a> hit a 20-foot jumper as time expired in game five at The Forum.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_games_in_the_1985&ndash;1986_NBA_season_and_playoffs_121-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_games_in_the_1985&ndash;1986_NBA_season_and_playoffs-121\">[121]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Prior to the <a title=\"1986&ndash;87 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1986&ndash;87 season</a>, the Lakers moved <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"A.C. Green\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A.C._Green\">A.C. Green</a> into the starting lineup, and acquired <a title=\"Mychal Thompson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mychal_Thompson\">Mychal Thompson</a> from the Spurs.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_History_#23_122-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_History_#23-122\">[122]</a></sup> Johnson won his first career MVP Award while leading the Lakers to a 65&ndash;17 record,<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_History_#23_122-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_History_#23-122\">[122]</a></sup> and Michael Cooper was named NBA Defensive Player of the Year.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_History_#23_122-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_History_#23-122\">[122]</a></sup> Before the season, Riley had made the decision to shift the focus of the offense to Johnson over the 40-year-old Abdul-Jabbar.<sup id=\"cite_ref-123\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-123\">[123]</a></sup> The Lakers advanced to the <a title=\"1987 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1987_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a> by sweeping the <a title=\"1986&ndash;87 Denver Nuggets season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_Denver_Nuggets_season\">Nuggets</a>, defeating the <a title=\"1986&ndash;87 Golden State Warriors season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_Golden_State_Warriors_season\">Warriors</a> in five games, and sweeping the <a title=\"1986&ndash;87 Seattle SuperSonics season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_Seattle_SuperSonics_season\">SuperSonics</a> in the <a title=\"1987 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1987_NBA_playoffs\">Western Conference Finals</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-124\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-124\">[124]</a></sup> The Lakers defeated <a title=\"1986&ndash;87 Boston Celtics season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_Boston_Celtics_season\">Boston</a> in the first two games of the Finals, and the teams split the next four games, giving Los Angeles their second championship in three seasons.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_History_#23_122-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_History_#23-122\">[122]</a></sup> The series was highlighted by Johnson's running \"baby hook\" shot to win game four at Boston Garden with two seconds remaining.<sup id=\"cite_ref-125\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-125\">[125]</a></sup> Johnson was named the NBA Finals MVP, in addition to regular season MVP.<sup id=\"cite_ref-126\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-126\">[126]</a></sup> At the Lakers' championship celebration in Los Angeles, coach Riley brashly declared that Los Angeles would repeat as NBA champions,<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_History_#23_122-4\" class=\"reference\"><a
