href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_History_#23-122\">[122]</a></sup> which no team had done since the <a title=\"1968&ndash;69 Boston Celtics season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1968%E2%80%9369_Boston_Celtics_season\">1968&ndash;69 Boston Celtics</a>.</p>\r\n<p>Looking to make good on Riley's promise in the <a title=\"1987&ndash;88 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1987&ndash;88 season</a>, the Lakers took their seventh consecutive Pacific Division title with a 62&ndash;20 record. They swept the <a title=\"1987&ndash;88 San Antonio Spurs season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_San_Antonio_Spurs_season\">Spurs</a> in the first round of the <a title=\"1988 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988_NBA_playoffs\">Western Conference Finals</a> before pulling out a tough seven-game series win over the <a title=\"1987&ndash;88 Utah Jazz season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_Utah_Jazz_season\">Utah Jazz</a> led by youngsters <a title=\"Karl Malone\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Malone\">Karl Malone</a> and <a title=\"John Stockton\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Stockton\">John Stockton</a>. A seven-game Western Conference finals win over the <a title=\"1987&ndash;88 Dallas Mavericks season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_Dallas_Mavericks_season\">Dallas Mavericks</a> propelled the Lakers to the <a title=\"1988 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a> once again. In their seventh trip to the Finals in nine years, they met the <a title=\"1987&ndash;88 Detroit Pistons season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_Detroit_Pistons_season\">Detroit Pistons</a>. Los Angeles would take the series in seven games, and James Worthy's game seven <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Triple-double\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triple-double\">triple-double</a> earned him a Finals MVP award.<sup id=\"cite_ref-127\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-127\">[127]</a></sup> The win marked their fifth title in nine years, but would also mark their last title until <a title=\"1999&ndash;2000 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">2000</a>.</p>\r\n<p>In the <a title=\"1988&ndash;89 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1988&ndash;89 season</a>, Los Angeles won 57 games and their eighth consecutive Pacific Division crown. They swept through the <a title=\"1989 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a> defeating <a title=\"1988&ndash;89 Portland Trail Blazers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_Portland_Trail_Blazers_season\">Portland</a>, <a title=\"1988&ndash;89 Seattle SuperSonics season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_Seattle_SuperSonics_season\">Seattle</a>, and <a title=\"1988&ndash;89 Phoenix Suns season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_Phoenix_Suns_season\">Phoenix</a>. In an eighth trip to the <a title=\"1989 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a> in 10 years, they once again faced the <a title=\"1988&ndash;89 Detroit Pistons season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988%E2%80%9389_Detroit_Pistons_season\">Detroit Pistons</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-128\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-128\">[128]</a></sup> Hampered by injuries to <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Byron Scott (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byron_Scott_(basketball)\">Byron Scott</a> and Johnson, the Lakers were swept by Detroit.<sup id=\"cite_ref-129\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-129\">[129]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Following the 1989 Finals, on June 28, 1989, after 20 professional seasons, Kareem Abdul-Jabbar announced his retirement. <a title=\"1989&ndash;90 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">The Lakers</a> still cruised through the Pacific Division, winning their ninth consecutive division crown with a 63&ndash;19 record. However, after beating the <a title=\"1989&ndash;90 Houston Rockets season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_Houston_Rockets_season\">Rockets</a> in the first round, they lost four games to one in the second round of the playoffs to the <a title=\"1989&ndash;90 Phoenix Suns season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_Phoenix_Suns_season\">Suns</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-130\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-130\">[130]</a></sup> Riley announced he was stepping down after the season citing <a title=\"Occupational burnout\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Occupational_burnout\">burnout</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-131\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-131\">[131]</a></sup> and was replaced by <a title=\"Mike Dunleavy Sr.\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Dunleavy_Sr.\">Mike Dunleavy</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lazenby._p._269_132-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lazenby._p._269-132\">[132]</a></sup> Riley's departure received a mixed reaction from the players. They respected his contributions, but some, such as Worthy and Scott, had grown tired of his intense practices and felt he tried to take too much credit for the team's successes.<sup id=\"cite_ref-133\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-133\">[133]</a></sup> Following the season, 1987 <a title=\"NBA Defensive Player of the Year Award\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Defensive_Player_of_the_Year_Award\">Defensive Player of the Year</a> winner <a title=\"Michael Cooper\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Cooper\">Michael Cooper</a> decided to play in Europe and was waived at his request.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lazenby,_p._269_134-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lazenby,_p._269-134\">[134]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The <a title=\"1990&ndash;91 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1990&ndash;91 Lakers</a> failed to win the Pacific Division for the first time in 10 years, but still finished with a 58&ndash;24 record. After cruising through the <a title=\"1991 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_NBA_playoffs\">Western Conference playoffs</a>, the Lakers found themselves in the <a title=\"1991 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a> once again, their ninth trip to the Finals in 12 years. The 1991 Finals represented a changing of the guard as the Lakers were defeated in five games by the <a title=\"1990&ndash;91 Chicago Bulls season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_Chicago_Bulls_season\">Chicago Bulls</a>, led by superstar <a title=\"Michael Jordan\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Jordan\">Michael Jordan</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-135\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-135\">[135]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1991.E2.80.931996:_Post-.22Showtime.22_dry_spell\"></span><span id=\"1991&ndash;1996:_Post-&quot;Showtime&quot;_dry_spell\" class=\"mw-headline\">1991&ndash;1996: Post-\"Showtime\" dry spell</span></h3>\r\n<p>On November 7, 1991, Magic Johnson announced he had tested positive for <a title=\"HIV\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HIV\">HIV</a> and would retire immediately.<sup id=\"cite_ref-136\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-136\">[136]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In their <a title=\"1991&ndash;92 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">first season</a> without Johnson, the team won 43 games to earn the eighth seed in the <a title=\"1992 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992_NBA_playoffs\">Western Conference playoffs</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL_32-5\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL-32\">[32]</a></sup> The Lakers were defeated in the first round by <a title=\"1991&ndash;92 Portland Trail Blazers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Portland_Trail_Blazers_season\">Portland</a>. Following the season, head coach Mike Dunleavy was fired.</p>\r\n<p>The Lakers would lose 43 games in <a title=\"1992&ndash;93 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1992&ndash;93</a> under <a title=\"Randy Pfund\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Randy_Pfund\">Randy Pfund</a>, their first losing season since 1976. The Lakers would still make the playoffs, and would become the first eighth seed to win the opening two games on the road against a number one seed when they took a 2&ndash;0 lead against <a title=\"1992&ndash;93 Phoenix Suns season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_Phoenix_Suns_season\">Phoenix</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-La3045_137-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-La3045-137\">[137]</a></sup> They lost the next two games at home however, then game five in Phoenix in overtime.<sup id=\"cite_ref-La3045_137-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-La3045-137\">[137]</a></sup> During the <a title=\"1993&ndash;94 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1993&ndash;94 season</a>, Pfund was fired during the season that would result in the Lakers failing to make the playoffs for the first time since 1976. Magic Johnson, would coach the final 16 games of the season with former teammate Michael Cooper as his lead assistant.<sup id=\"cite_ref-138\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-138\">[138]</a></sup> Johnson decided not to take the job permanently due to what he felt was a lack of commitment from certain players, and Los Angeles ended the season with a 10-game losing streak to finish 33&ndash;49.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lazenby,_p._307_139-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lazenby,_p._307-139\">[139]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-140\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-140\">[140]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Under new coach <a title=\"Del Harris\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Del_Harris\">Del Harris</a>, Los Angeles made the playoffs each of the next two seasons but was eliminated in the second and first rounds respectively.<sup id=\"cite_ref-141\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-141\">[141]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-142\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-142\">[142]</a></sup> The team was led by young guards <a title=\"Nick Van Exel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nick_Van_Exel\">Nick Van Exel</a> and <a title=\"Eddie Jones (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eddie_Jones_(basketball)\">Eddie Jones</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lazenby._p._307_143-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lazenby._p._307-143\">[143]</a></sup> Johnson came out of retirement to return as a player in the <a title=\"1995&ndash;96 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1995&ndash;96 season</a> to lead the then 24&ndash;18 Lakers to a 29&ndash;11 finish.<sup id=\"cite_ref-144\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-144\">[144]</a></sup> After some run-ins with Van Exel, displeasure with Harris's strategies, and a first-round loss to the <a title=\"1995&ndash;96 Houston Rockets season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_Houston_Rockets_season\">Rockets</a>, Johnson decided to retire for the final time after the season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-145\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-145\">[145]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"1996.E2.80.932004:_O.27Neal_and_Bryant_dynasty\"></span><span id=\"1996&ndash;2004:_O'Neal_and_Bryant_dynasty\" class=\"mw-headline\">1996&ndash;2004: O'Neal and Bryant dynasty</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 242px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lakers_banners_%26_retired_jerseys_2022.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Lakers_banners_%26_retired_jerseys_2022.jpg/240px-Lakers_banners_%26_retired_jerseys_2022.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Lakers_banners_%26_retired_jerseys_2022.jpg/360px-Lakers_banners_%26_retired_jerseys_2022.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Lakers_banners_%26_retired_jerseys_2022.jpg/480px-Lakers_banners_%26_retired_jerseys_2022.jpg 2x\" width=\"240\" height=\"116\" data-file-width=\"3822\" data-file-height=\"1849\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 242px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">Championship banners from Minneapolis and Los Angeles &amp; retired jerseys, hanging in the rafters of Crypto.com Arena in 2022</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>During the 1996 off-season, the Lakers acquired 17-year-old <a title=\"Kobe Bryant\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kobe_Bryant\">Kobe Bryant</a> from the <a title=\"Charlotte Hornets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlotte_Hornets\">Charlotte Hornets</a> for <a title=\"Vlade Divac\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vlade_Divac\">Vlade Divac</a>; Bryant was drafted 13th overall out of <a title=\"Lower Merion High School\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_Merion_High_School\">Lower Merion High School</a> in <a title=\"Ardmore, Pennsylvania\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ardmore,_Pennsylvania\">Ardmore, Pennsylvania</a> in <a title=\"1996 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1996_NBA_draft\">that year's draft</a>, by Charlotte. Los Angeles also signed free-agent <a title=\"Shaquille O'Neal\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaquille_O%27Neal\">Shaquille O'Neal</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-146\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-146\">[146]</a></sup> Trading for Bryant was West's idea, and he was influential in the team's signing of the all-star center.<sup id=\"cite_ref-147\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-147\">[147]</a></sup> \"Jerry West is the reason I came to the Lakers\", O'Neal later said.<sup id=\"cite_ref-148\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-148\">[148]</a></sup> They used their 24th pick in the draft to select <a title=\"Derek Fisher\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Derek_Fisher\">Derek Fisher</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-149\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-149\">[149]</a></sup> During <a title=\"1996&ndash;97 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">the season</a>, the team traded <a title=\"Cedric Ceballos\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cedric_Ceballos\">Cedric Ceballos</a> to Phoenix for <a title=\"Robert Horry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Horry\">Robert Horry</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Dynasty_No._5:_Los_Angeles_Lakers_150-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Dynasty_No._5:_Los_Angeles_Lakers-150\">[150]</a></sup> O'Neal led the team to a 56&ndash;26 record, their best effort since 1990&ndash;91, despite missing 31 games due to a knee injury.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_96_151-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_96-151\">[151]</a></sup> O'Neal averaged 26.2&nbsp;ppg and 12.5&nbsp;rpg and finished third in the league in blocked shots (2.88&nbsp;bpg) in 51 games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_96_151-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_96-151\">[151]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-152\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-152\">[152]</a></sup> The Lakers defeated the <a title=\"1996&ndash;97 Portland Trail Blazers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_Portland_Trail_Blazers_season\">Portland Trail Blazers</a> in the first round of the <a title=\"1997 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1997_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a> as O'Neal scored 46 points in Game&nbsp;1 against the Trail Blazers, marking the highest single-game playoff scoring output by a Laker since Jerry West scored 53 against the Celtics in 1969.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_96_151-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_96-151\">[151]</a></sup> In the next round, the Lakers lost in five games to the <a title=\"1996&ndash;97 Utah Jazz season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_Utah_Jazz_season\">Utah Jazz</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_96_151-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_96-151\">[151]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In the <a title=\"1997&ndash;98 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1997&ndash;98 season</a>, O'Neal and the Lakers had the best start in franchise history, 11&ndash;0.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_History_#33_153-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_History_#33-153\">[153]</a></sup> O'Neal would miss 20 games on the season due to an abdominal injury.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_History_#33_153-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_History_#33-153\">[153]</a></sup> Los Angeles battled <a title=\"1997&ndash;98 Seattle SuperSonics season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_Seattle_SuperSonics_season\">Seattle</a> for the Pacific Division title most of the season. In the final two months, the Lakers won 22 of their final 25 games,<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_History_#33_153-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_History_#33-153\">[153]</a></sup> finishing 61&ndash;21, but still finished second to Seattle in the standings.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_History_#33_153-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_History_#33-153\">[153]</a></sup> The Lakers defeated <a title=\"1997&ndash;98 Portland Trail Blazers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_Portland_Trail_Blazers_season\">Portland</a> three games to one in the first round to advance to face Seattle. Although the Sonics won the first game, the Lakers responded with four straight wins, taking the series,<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_History_#33_153-4\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_History_#33-153\">[153]</a></sup> but were swept by the <a title=\"1997&ndash;98 Utah Jazz season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_Utah_Jazz_season\">Jazz</a> in the <a title=\"1998 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_NBA_playoffs\">Western Conference Finals</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_History_#33_153-5\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_History_#33-153\">[153]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>During the <a title=\"1998&ndash;99 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1998&ndash;99 season</a>, All-Star guard <a title=\"Eddie Jones (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eddie_Jones_(basketball)\">Eddie Jones</a> and center <a title=\"Elden Campbell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elden_Campbell\">Elden Campbell</a> were traded to the Charlotte Hornets.<sup id=\"cite_ref-154\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-154\">[154]</a></sup> The team also acquired <a title=\"J. R. Reid\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._R._Reid\">J. R. Reid</a>, <a title=\"B. J. Armstrong\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B._J._Armstrong\">B. J. Armstrong</a>, and <a title=\"Glen Rice\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glen_Rice\">Glen Rice</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-155\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-155\">[155]</a></sup> Head coach Del Harris was fired in February after a three-game losing streak and replaced on an interim basis by former Laker <a title=\"Kurt Rambis\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurt_Rambis\">Kurt Rambis</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-156\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-156\">[156]</a></sup> The team finished 31&ndash;19 in the strike-shortened season, which was fourth in the Western Conference.<sup id=\"cite_ref-157\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-157\">[157]</a></sup> The Lakers defeated <a title=\"1998&ndash;99 Houston Rockets season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_Houston_Rockets_season\">Houston</a> in the first round of the playoffs, but were swept by <a title=\"1998&ndash;99 San Antonio Spurs season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_San_Antonio_Spurs_season\">San Antonio</a> in the next round. Game four of the series would be the last game ever played at the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"The Forum (Inglewood, California)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Forum_(Inglewood,_California)\">Great Western Forum</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-158\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-158\">[158]</a></sup></p>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tleft\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 222px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Shaq_at_the_white_house.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Shaq_at_the_white_house.jpg/220px-Shaq_at_the_white_house.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Shaq_at_the_white_house.jpg/330px-Shaq_at_the_white_house.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Shaq_at_the_white_house.jpg/440px-Shaq_at_the_white_house.jpg 2x\" width=\"220\" height=\"159\" data-file-width=\"600\" data-file-height=\"433\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tleft\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 222px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">The Lakers at the <a title=\"White House\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House\">White House</a> following their 2001 NBA championship</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>Before the <a title=\"1999&ndash;2000 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_NBA_season\">1999&ndash;2000 season</a>, West was prepared to hire Rambis as the team's full-time coach before an outcry from fans and members of the organization caused him to seek out a bigger name.<sup id=\"cite_ref-159\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-159\">[159]</a></sup> Los Angeles hired former <a title=\"Chicago Bulls\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago_Bulls\">Chicago Bulls</a> coach <a title=\"Phil Jackson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phil_Jackson\">Phil Jackson</a>, who had coached that team to six championships, and gave him a lucrative $6&nbsp;million a year contract.<sup id=\"cite_ref-160\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-160\">[160]</a></sup> He brought along assistant <a title=\"Tex Winter\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tex_Winter\">Tex Winter</a> and they installed Winter's version of the <a title=\"Triangle offense\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triangle_offense\">triangle offense</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-161\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-161\">[161]</a></sup> The Lakers signed veterans <a title=\"Brian Shaw\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Shaw\">Brian Shaw</a>, <a title=\"John Salley\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Salley\">John Salley</a>, <a title=\"Ron Harper\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ron_Harper\">Ron Harper</a>, and <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"A.C. Green\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A.C._Green\">A.C. Green</a>, who was a Laker during the \"Showtime\" era.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Dynasty_No._5:_Los_Angeles_Lakers_150-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Dynasty_No._5:_Los_Angeles_Lakers-150\">[150]</a></sup> The team also moved to a new arena, the Staples Center.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#35_162-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#35-162\">[162]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Led by league MVP O'Neal, the <a title=\"1999&ndash;2000 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">Lakers</a> won 31 of their first 36 games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_1999&ndash;2000_Summary_163-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_1999&ndash;2000_Summary-163\">[163]</a></sup> They finished 67&ndash;15, the highest win total since they won 65 in the <a title=\"1986&ndash;87 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1986&ndash;87 season</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_1999&ndash;2000_Summary_163-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_1999&ndash;2000_Summary-163\">[163]</a></sup> The eliminated <a title=\"1999&ndash;2000 Sacramento Kings season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Sacramento_Kings_season\">Sacramento</a> and <a title=\"1999&ndash;2000 Phoenix Suns season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Phoenix_Suns_season\">Phoenix</a> in the first two rounds of the <a title=\"2000 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-164\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-164\">[164]</a></sup> After the Lakers took a three games to one lead in the Western Conference Finals against <a title=\"1999&ndash;2000 Portland Trail Blazers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Portland_Trail_Blazers_season\">Portland</a>, the Trail Blazers won the next two games to force a game seven.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Blazers'_dry_spell_allows_Lakers_to_take_Game_7_165-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Blazers'_dry_spell_allows_Lakers_to_take_Game_7-165\">[165]</a></sup> The Lakers, who trailed by 15 points in the fourth quarter, would go on 19&ndash;4 run to tie the game and eventually win 89&ndash;84 to advance to the <a title=\"2000 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Blazers'_dry_spell_allows_Lakers_to_take_Game_7_165-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Blazers'_dry_spell_allows_Lakers_to_take_Game_7-165\">[165]</a></sup> In their first trip to the Finals since <a title=\"1991 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_NBA_Finals\">1991</a>, the Lakers defeated <a title=\"Reggie Miller\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reggie_Miller\">Reggie Miller</a> and the <a title=\"1999&ndash;2000 Indiana Pacers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Indiana_Pacers_season\">Indiana Pacers</a> four games to two win their first title since <a title=\"1987&ndash;88 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1988</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-166\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-166\">[166]</a></sup> West retired from his spot in the team's front office after the season after a power struggle between him and Jackson over control of the team's operations.<sup id=\"cite_ref-167\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-167\">[167]</a></sup> After the season, starters Rice and Green left the team,<sup id=\"cite_ref-168\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-168\">[168]</a></sup> and Los Angeles signed <a title=\"Horace Grant\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horace_Grant\">Horace Grant</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-169\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-169\">[169]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The <a title=\"2000&ndash;01 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">following season</a>, the Lakers won 11 fewer regular season games than the prior year,<sup id=\"cite_ref-170\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-170\">[170]</a></sup> but swept the first three rounds of the <a title=\"2001 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a>, defeating the <a title=\"2000&ndash;01 Portland Trail Blazers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Portland_Trail_Blazers_season\">Portland</a>, <a title=\"2000&ndash;01 Sacramento Kings season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Sacramento_Kings_season\">Sacramento</a>, and <a title=\"2000&ndash;01 San Antonio Spurs season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_San_Antonio_Spurs_season\">San Antonio</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-171\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-171\">[171]</a></sup> They met <a title=\"Allen Iverson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allen_Iverson\">Allen Iverson</a> and the <a title=\"2000&ndash;01 Philadelphia 76ers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Philadelphia_76ers_season\">Philadelphia 76ers</a> in the <a title=\"2001 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a>. Although the Sixers took game one in overtime,<sup id=\"cite_ref-172\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-172\">[172]</a></sup> the Lakers won the next four games to win their second straight title. Their 15&ndash;1 postseason record was the best in NBA history.<sup id=\"cite_ref-173\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-173\">[173]</a></sup></p>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tmulti tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner multiimageinner\" style=\"width: 304px; max-width: 304px;\">\r\n<div class=\"trow\">\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 149px; max-width: 149px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lipofsky_Shaquille_O%27Neal.jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Lipofsky_Shaquille_O%27Neal.jpg/147px-Lipofsky_Shaquille_O%27Neal.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/Lipofsky_Shaquille_O%27Neal.jpg 1.5x\" alt=\"\" width=\"147\" height=\"222\" data-file-width=\"199\" data-file-height=\"300\"></a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 151px; max-width: 151px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lipofsky_Kobe.jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lipofsky_Kobe.jpg/149px-Lipofsky_Kobe.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e0/Lipofsky_Kobe.jpg 1.5x\" alt=\"\" width=\"149\" height=\"222\" data-file-width=\"201\" data-file-height=\"300\"></a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"trow\" style=\"display: flex;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Shaquille O'Neal\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaquille_O%27Neal\">Shaquille O'Neal</a> (left), and <a title=\"Kobe Bryant\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kobe_Bryant\">Kobe Bryant</a> (right), helped the Lakers win three straight NBA titles. Though they played well together on the court, the pair had an acrimonious relationship at times in the locker room.<sup id=\"cite_ref-174\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-174\">[174]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-175\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-175\">[175]</a></sup></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>The Lakers won 58 games in <a title=\"2001&ndash;02 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_NBA_season\">2001&ndash;02</a>. In the <a title=\"2002 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a>, they swept <a title=\"2001&ndash;02 Portland Trail Blazers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_Portland_Trail_Blazers_season\">Portland</a> and defeated <a title=\"2000&ndash;01 San Antonio Spurs season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_San_Antonio_Spurs_season\">San Antonio</a> four games to one to advance to the Western Conference Finals to face <a title=\"2001&ndash;02 Sacramento Kings season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_Sacramento_Kings_season\">Sacramento</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-2002_ballref_176-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-2002_ballref-176\">[176]</a></sup> The series would go on to be known as one of the greatest playoff matchups in NBA history. The series extended to all seven games and ended in a Lakers victory.<sup id=\"cite_ref-177\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-177\">[177]</a></sup> In game one, Bryant scored 30 points as the Lakers won, 106&ndash;99. The series would then shift in Sacramento's favor, with the Kings winning the next two games. Facing a deficit in game 4, the Lakers had the ball with under 20 seconds to play. After misses by both Bryant and O'Neal, Kings center <a title=\"Vlade Divac\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vlade_Divac\">Vlade Divac</a> tapped the ball away from the rim in an attempt to wind down the clock. It went straight into <a title=\"Robert Horry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Horry\">Robert Horry</a>'s hands, who drained a game-winning three with under three seconds to play. After the Kings won game five on a buzzer-beater by <a title=\"Mike Bibby\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Bibby\">Mike Bibby</a>, the Lakers were faced with a must-win game six. In one of the most controversial playoff games in league history (<a title=\"Tim Donaghy\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tim_Donaghy\">Tim Donaghy</a>'s <a title=\"2007 NBA betting scandal\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2007_NBA_betting_scandal\">betting scandal</a>), the Lakers would win by four points.<sup id=\"cite_ref-178\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-178\">[178]</a></sup> The Lakers went on to win game seven in overtime, with the Kings missing numerous potentially game-saving shots and free throws. The Lakers then achieved a three-peat by sweeping <a title=\"Jason Kidd\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jason_Kidd\">Jason Kidd</a> and the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"New Jersey Nets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Jersey_Nets\">New Jersey Nets</a> in the <a title=\"2002 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-179\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-179\">[179]</a></sup> O'Neal won each of the Finals series' MVP awards, making him the only player besides <a title=\"Michael Jordan\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Jordan\">Michael Jordan</a> to win three consecutive Finals MVPs.<sup id=\"cite_ref-finalsmvp_180-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-finalsmvp-180\">[180]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The <a title=\"2002&ndash;03 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">Lakers</a> would attempt a four-peat the following year, but started the <a title=\"2002&ndash;03 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_NBA_season\">2002&ndash;03 season</a> 11&ndash;19.<sup id=\"cite_ref-181\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-181\">[181]</a></sup> However, they finished the season 39&ndash;13 to finish 50&ndash;32.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_2002&ndash;03_Summary_182-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_2002&ndash;03_Summary-182\">[182]</a></sup> They defeated <a title=\"2002&ndash;03 Minnesota Timberwolves season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Minnesota_Timberwolves_season\">Minnesota</a> in the first round of the <a title=\"2003 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a>, but the four-peat attempt ended as they were eliminated by <a title=\"2002&ndash;03 San Antonio Spurs season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_San_Antonio_Spurs_season\">San Antonio</a> in six games in the second round.<sup id=\"cite_ref-183\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-183\">[183]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>During the <a title=\"2003&ndash;04 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">2003&ndash;04 season</a>, the team was the subject of intense media coverage generated by the teaming of four stars and the <a title=\"Kobe Bryant sexual assault case\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kobe_Bryant_sexual_assault_case\">sexual-assault case involving Kobe Bryant</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-184\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-184\">[184]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-185\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-185\">[185]</a></sup> Before the season, the Lakers signed two-time MVP <a title=\"Karl Malone\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Malone\">Karl Malone</a> formerly of the <a title=\"Utah Jazz\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utah_Jazz\">Jazz</a>, and former <a title=\"Seattle SuperSonics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seattle_SuperSonics\">Seattle</a> Defensive Player of the Year <a title=\"Gary Payton\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gary_Payton\">Gary Payton</a> to join O'Neal and Bryant.<sup id=\"cite_ref-186\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-186\">[186]</a></sup> Three of the \"big four\", however, struggled with injuries: O'Neal suffered from a strained calf, Malone an injured knee, and Bryant an injured shoulder.<sup id=\"cite_ref-187\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-187\">[187]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-188\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-188\">[188]</a></sup> The Lakers started 18&ndash;3 and finished 56&ndash;26 and won the <a title=\"Pacific Division (NBA)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_Division_(NBA)\">Pacific Division</a> title, entering the <a title=\"2004 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a> as the No. 2 seed. They defeated <a title=\"2003&ndash;04 Houston Rockets season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Houston_Rockets_season\">Houston</a>, <a title=\"2003&ndash;04 San Antonio Spurs season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_San_Antonio_Spurs_season\">San Antonio</a>, and <a title=\"2003&ndash;04 Minnesota Timberwolves season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Minnesota_Timberwolves_season\">Minnesota</a> to advance to the <a title=\"2004 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-189\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-189\">[189]</a></sup> In the Finals, they would lose to <a title=\"2003&ndash;04 Detroit Pistons season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Detroit_Pistons_season\">Detroit</a> in five games.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"2004.E2.80.932016:_The_Kobe_Bryant_era\"></span><span id=\"2004&ndash;2016:_The_Kobe_Bryant_era\" class=\"mw-headline\">2004&ndash;2016: The Kobe Bryant era</span></h3>\r\n<h4><span id=\"2004.E2.80.932007:_Rebuilding\"></span><span id=\"2004&ndash;2007:_Rebuilding\" class=\"mw-headline\">2004&ndash;2007: Rebuilding</span></h4>\r\n<p>During the 2004 off-season, the team entered a rebuilding phase when O'Neal was traded to the <a title=\"Miami Heat\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miami_Heat\">Miami Heat</a> for <a title=\"Lamar Odom\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lamar_Odom\">Lamar Odom</a>, <a title=\"Brian Grant\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Grant\">Brian Grant</a>, <a title=\"Caron Butler\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caron_Butler\">Caron Butler</a>, and a first-round draft pick.<sup id=\"cite_ref-190\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-190\">[190]</a></sup> Bryant and O'Neal had <a title=\"Shaq&ndash;Kobe feud\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaq%E2%80%93Kobe_feud\">clashed in the past</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-191\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-191\">[191]</a></sup> and the media credited their feud as one of the motivating factors for the trade.<sup id=\"cite_ref-192\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-192\">[192]</a></sup> Jackson did not return as head coach, and <a title=\"The Last Season: A Team in Search of Its Soul\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Last_Season:_A_Team_in_Search_of_Its_Soul\">wrote a book</a> about the team's 2003&ndash;04 season, in which he heavily criticized Bryant and called him \"uncoachable\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-193\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-193\">[193]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-194\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-194\">[194]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-195\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-195\">[195]</a></sup> The Lakers front office said that the book contained \"several inaccuracies\".<sup id=\"cite_ref-196\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-196\">[196]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Lakers also traded <a title=\"Rick Fox\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rick_Fox\">Rick Fox</a> and Gary Payton to Boston, for <a title=\"Chris Mihm\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Mihm\">Chris Mihm</a>, <a title=\"Marcus Banks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marcus_Banks\">Marcus Banks</a>, and <a title=\"Chucky Atkins\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chucky_Atkins\">Chucky Atkins</a> before the <a title=\"2004&ndash;05 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_NBA_season\">2004&ndash;05 season</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-L.A._gets_Mihm,_Banks,_Atkins_in_deal_197-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-L.A._gets_Mihm,_Banks,_Atkins_in_deal-197\">[197]</a></sup> Derek Fisher, frustrated with losing playing time, opted out of his contract and signed with the Warriors.<sup id=\"cite_ref-L.A._gets_Mihm,_Banks,_Atkins_in_deal_197-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-L.A._gets_Mihm,_Banks,_Atkins_in_deal-197\">[197]</a></sup> The team hired <a title=\"Rudy Tomjanovich\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rudy_Tomjanovich\">Rudy Tomjanovich</a> to replace Jackson.<sup id=\"cite_ref-L.A._gets_Mihm,_Banks,_Atkins_in_deal_197-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-L.A._gets_Mihm,_Banks,_Atkins_in_deal-197\">[197]</a></sup> After sitting out the first half of the <a title=\"2004&ndash;05 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">2004&ndash;05 season</a>, Malone announced his retirement on February 13, 2005.<sup id=\"cite_ref-198\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-198\">[198]</a></sup> Tomjanovich coached the team to a 22&ndash;19 record before resigning due to health problems.<sup id=\"cite_ref-199\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-199\">[199]</a></sup> Assistant <a title=\"Frank Hamblen\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Hamblen\">Frank Hamblen</a> was named interim head coach to replace Tomjanovich for the remainder of the season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-200\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-200\">[200]</a></sup> Bryant (ankle) and Odom (shoulder) suffered injuries, and the Lakers finished 34&ndash;48, missing the playoffs for only the fifth time in franchise history and the first time since <a title=\"1993&ndash;94 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">1994</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL_32-6\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL-32\">[32]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>With the tenth overall pick in the <a title=\"2005 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005_NBA_draft\">2005 NBA draft</a>, the Lakers selected <a title=\"Andrew Bynum\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Bynum\">Andrew Bynum</a>, a center from <a title=\"St. Joseph High School (Metuchen, New Jersey)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Joseph_High_School_(Metuchen,_New_Jersey)\">St. Joseph High School</a> in <a title=\"Metuchen, New Jersey\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metuchen,_New_Jersey\">Metuchen, New Jersey</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-201\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-201\">[201]</a></sup> The team also traded Caron Butler and Chucky Atkins to <a title=\"Washington Wizards\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_Wizards\">Washington</a> for <a title=\"Kwame Brown\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kwame_Brown\">Kwame Brown</a> and <a title=\"Laron Profit\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laron_Profit\">Laron Profit</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-202\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-202\">[202]</a></sup> Jackson returned to coach the <a title=\"2005&ndash;06 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">team</a> after Rudy Tomjanovich resigned midway through the previous season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-203\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-203\">[203]</a></sup> On January 22, 2006, Bryant scored 81 points against <a title=\"2005&ndash;06 Toronto Raptors season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Toronto_Raptors_season\">Toronto</a>, the second-highest total in NBA history.<sup id=\"cite_ref-204\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-204\">[204]</a></sup> Ending the season 45&ndash;37, the team made the <a title=\"2005 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a> after a one-season absence.<sup id=\"cite_ref-205\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-205\">[205]</a></sup> After taking a three games to one lead in the first round, <a title=\"2005&ndash;06 Phoenix Suns season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Phoenix_Suns_season\">Phoenix</a> came back to take the series in seven games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-206\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-206\">[206]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In <a title=\"2005&ndash;06 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">the following season</a>, the Lakers won 26 of their first 39 games,<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_2006&ndash;07_Summary_207-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_2006&ndash;07_Summary-207\">[207]</a></sup> but lost 27 of their last 43&mdash;including seven in a row at one point&mdash;to finish 42&ndash;40.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_2006&ndash;07_Summary_207-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_2006&ndash;07_Summary-207\">[207]</a></sup> They were eliminated in the <a title=\"2006 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006_NBA_playoffs\">first round</a> by <a title=\"2005&ndash;06 Phoenix Suns season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Phoenix_Suns_season\">Phoenix</a> again.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_2006&ndash;07_Summary_207-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_2006&ndash;07_Summary-207\">[207]</a></sup> Frustrated by the team's inability to advance in the playoffs, Bryant demanded to be traded in the off-season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-208\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-208\">[208]</a></sup> Buss initially agreed to seek a trade,<sup id=\"cite_ref-209\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-209\">[209]</a></sup> but also worked to try to change Bryant's mind.<sup id=\"cite_ref-210\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-210\">[210]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h4><span id=\"2007.E2.80.932011:_Bryant_and_Gasol_duo\"></span><span id=\"2007&ndash;2011:_Bryant_and_Gasol_duo\" class=\"mw-headline\">2007&ndash;2011: Bryant and Gasol duo</span></h4>\r\n<p>After re-acquiring <a title=\"Derek Fisher\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Derek_Fisher\">Derek Fisher</a>, the Lakers started the <a title=\"2007&ndash;08 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_NBA_season\">2007&ndash;08 season</a> with a 25&ndash;11 record, before <a title=\"Andrew Bynum\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andrew_Bynum\">Andrew Bynum</a>, their center who was leading the league in field-goal percentage, went out for the year due to a knee injury in mid-January.<sup id=\"cite_ref-211\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-211\">[211]</a></sup> In what would become a crucial transfer for the franchise's return to championship form, they acquired the six-time all-star power forward <a title=\"Pau Gasol\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pau_Gasol\">Pau Gasol</a> from the <a title=\"Memphis Grizzlies\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memphis_Grizzlies\">Memphis Grizzlies</a> in a trade in early February and went 22&ndash;5 to finish the season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-212\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-212\">[212]</a></sup> The Lakers' 57&ndash;25 record earned them the first seed in the <a title=\"Western Conference (NBA)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Conference_(NBA)\">Western Conference</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-213\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-213\">[213]</a></sup> Bryant was awarded the league's MVP award, becoming the first Laker to win the award since O'Neal in 2000.<sup id=\"cite_ref-214\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-214\">[214]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-215\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-215\">[215]</a></sup> In <a title=\"2008 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_NBA_playoffs\">the playoffs</a>, they defeated the Nuggets in four games, the Jazz in six, and the defending champion Spurs in five, but lost to the <a title=\"Boston Celtics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics\">Celtics</a> in six games in <a title=\"2008 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_NBA_Finals\">the NBA Finals</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-216\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-216\">[216]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In the <a title=\"2008&ndash;09 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_NBA_season\">2008&ndash;09 season</a>, the Lakers finished 65&ndash;17; the best record in the Western Conference.<sup id=\"cite_ref-217\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-217\">[217]</a></sup> They defeated the <a title=\"Utah Jazz\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utah_Jazz\">Jazz</a> in five games, the <a title=\"Houston Rockets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houston_Rockets\">Rockets</a> in seven and the <a title=\"Denver Nuggets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denver_Nuggets\">Nuggets</a> in six, to win the Western Conference title. They then won their 15th NBA championship by defeating the <a title=\"Orlando Magic\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orlando_Magic\">Orlando Magic</a> in five games in <a title=\"2009 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_NBA_Finals\">the NBA finals</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-218\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-218\">[218]</a></sup> Bryant was named the NBA Finals MVP for the first time in his career.<sup id=\"cite_ref-219\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-219\">[219]</a></sup></p>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 222px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2010_NBA_Champion_Los_Angeles_Lakers_with_President_Obama.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/2010_NBA_Champion_Los_Angeles_Lakers_with_President_Obama.jpg/220px-2010_NBA_Champion_Los_Angeles_Lakers_with_President_Obama.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/2010_NBA_Champion_Los_Angeles_Lakers_with_President_Obama.jpg/330px-2010_NBA_Champion_Los_Angeles_Lakers_with_President_Obama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/2010_NBA_Champion_Los_Angeles_Lakers_with_President_Obama.jpg/440px-2010_NBA_Champion_Los_Angeles_Lakers_with_President_Obama.jpg 2x\" width=\"220\" height=\"147\" data-file-width=\"1600\" data-file-height=\"1066\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 222px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">The Lakers with President <a title=\"Barack Obama\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama\">Barack Obama</a> following their 2010 NBA championship</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>The Lakers, who had added <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Ron Artest\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ron_Artest\">Ron Artest</a> (now Metta World Peace)<sup id=\"cite_ref-220\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-220\">[220]</a></sup> in place of <a title=\"Trevor Ariza\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trevor_Ariza\">Trevor Ariza</a> in their starting lineup, finished <a title=\"2009&ndash;10 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_NBA_season\">the 2009&ndash;10 season</a> with the best record in the <a title=\"Western Conference (NBA)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Conference_(NBA)\">Western Conference</a> for the third straight time. On January 13, 2010, the Lakers became the first team in NBA history to win 3,000 regular-season games by defeating the <a title=\"Dallas Mavericks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dallas_Mavericks\">Dallas Mavericks</a> 100&ndash;95.<sup id=\"cite_ref-221\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-221\">[221]</a></sup> They defeated the <a title=\"Oklahoma City Thunder\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oklahoma_City_Thunder\">Oklahoma City Thunder</a>, the <a title=\"Utah Jazz\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utah_Jazz\">Utah Jazz</a>, and the <a title=\"Phoenix Suns\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phoenix_Suns\">Phoenix Suns</a> in the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"NBA Playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Playoffs\">Western Conference playoffs</a>. In <a title=\"2010 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_NBA_Finals\">the finals</a>, the Lakers played the <a title=\"Boston Celtics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics\">Boston Celtics</a> for the 12th time. They rallied back from a 3&ndash;2 disadvantage in the series and erased a 13-point deficit in the fourth quarter of the seventh game to defeat the Celtics. This series win gave them their 16th NBA title overall and 11th since they moved to Los Angeles.<sup id=\"cite_ref-222\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-222\">[222]</a></sup> Bryant was named Finals MVP for the second year in a row, despite a 6&ndash;24 shooting performance in game seven.<sup id=\"cite_ref-223\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-223\">[223]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>After much speculation, head coach Phil Jackson returned for the <a title=\"2010&ndash;11 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_NBA_season\">2010&ndash;11 season</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-224\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-224\">[224]</a></sup> In the <a title=\"2011 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a>, the Lakers defeated the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"New Orleans Hornets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Orleans_Hornets\">New Orleans Hornets</a> in the first round.<sup id=\"cite_ref-225\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-225\">[225]</a></sup> But their opportunity for a three-peat was denied by the <a title=\"Dallas Mavericks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dallas_Mavericks\">Dallas Mavericks</a> in a four-game sweep of the second round. After the season, it was announced that Jackson will not be returning to coach the Lakers.<sup id=\"cite_ref-226\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-226\">[226]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h4><span id=\"2011.E2.80.932016:_Post-Jackson_era\"></span><span id=\"2011&ndash;2016:_Post-Jackson_era\" class=\"mw-headline\">2011&ndash;2016: Post-Jackson era</span></h4>\r\n<p>After Jackson's retirement, former <a title=\"Cleveland Cavaliers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cleveland_Cavaliers\">Cleveland Cavaliers</a> head coach <a title=\"Mike Brown (basketball, born 1970)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Brown_(basketball,_born_1970)\">Mike Brown</a> was hired as head coach on May 25, 2011.<sup id=\"cite_ref-227\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-227\">[227]</a></sup> Before the start of the <a title=\"2011 NBA lockout\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_NBA_lockout\">shortened</a> <a title=\"2011&ndash;12 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_NBA_season\">2011&ndash;12</a> season, the Lakers traded <a title=\"Lamar Odom\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lamar_Odom\">Lamar Odom</a> to the <a title=\"Dallas Mavericks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dallas_Mavericks\">Dallas Mavericks</a> after Odom requested to be traded.<sup id=\"cite_ref-228\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-228\">[228]</a></sup> On the trade deadline long time Laker <a title=\"Derek Fisher\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Derek_Fisher\">Derek Fisher</a> along with a first round draft pick were traded to the <a title=\"Houston Rockets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houston_Rockets\">Houston Rockets</a> for <a title=\"Jordan Hill (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_Hill_(basketball)\">Jordan Hill</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-229\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-229\">[229]</a></sup> With a 41&ndash;25 regular season record the Lakers entered the <a title=\"2012 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a> as the third seed, the team defeated the <a title=\"Denver Nuggets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denver_Nuggets\">Denver Nuggets</a> in the first round in seven games but were eliminated by the <a title=\"Oklahoma City Thunder\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oklahoma_City_Thunder\">Oklahoma City Thunder</a> in the second round in five games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-230\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-230\">[230]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-231\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-231\">[231]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>On July 4, 2012, <a title=\"Steve Nash\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Nash\">Steve Nash</a> of the Phoenix Suns agreed to a <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Sign and trade\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sign_and_trade\">sign-and-trade</a> deal that would send him to the Lakers in exchange for the Lakers' 2013 and 2015 first round draft picks, 2013 and 2014 second round draft picks, and $3&nbsp;million. The trade was made official on July 11, 2012, the first day the trade moratorium was lifted.<sup id=\"cite_ref-232\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-232\">[232]</a></sup> On August 10, 2012, in a four-team trade the Lakers traded Andrew Bynum and acquired <a title=\"Dwight Howard\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwight_Howard\">Dwight Howard</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-233\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-233\">[233]</a></sup> On November 9, 2012, Mike Brown was relieved of coaching duties after a 1&ndash;4 start to the <a title=\"2012&ndash;13 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">2012&ndash;13</a> season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-234\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-234\">[234]</a></sup> Assistant Coach Bernie Bickerstaff took over as interim head coach, leading the Lakers to a 5&ndash;5 record. On November 12, 2012, the Lakers hired <a title=\"Mike D'Antoni\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_D%27Antoni\">Mike D'Antoni</a> as head coach.<sup id=\"cite_ref-235\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-235\">[235]</a></sup> On February 18, 2013, Lakers owner Jerry Buss died from cancer at age 80.<sup id=\"cite_ref-236\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-236\">[236]</a></sup> On the court, D'Antoni coached the Lakers to a 40&ndash;32 record the rest of the way to finish 45&ndash;37, their worst record since <a title=\"2006&ndash;07 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_NBA_season\">2007</a>. The Lakers clinched a playoff berth on the final game of the season and finished seventh in the Western Conference after beating the Houston Rockets on April 16, 2013.<sup id=\"cite_ref-237\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-237\">[237]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-238\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-238\">[238]</a></sup> The Lakers battled injuries all season, the most prominent of which is the <a title=\"Achilles tendon rupture\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achilles_tendon_rupture\">Achilles tendon rupture</a> to Kobe Bryant that ended his season after 78 games. The absence of Bryant was sorely felt as the Lakers were swept by the San Antonio Spurs in the first round of the <a title=\"2013 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013_NBA_playoffs\">2013 NBA playoffs</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-239\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-239\">[239]</a></sup> Nevertheless, Bryant passed Lakers legend Wilt Chamberlain to become the fourth all-time leading scorer in NBA history on March 30, 2013, against the Sacramento Kings.<sup id=\"cite_ref-240\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-240\">[240]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>On December 8, 2013, Bryant played in his first game since tearing his Achilles tendon on April 12, 2013.<sup id=\"cite_ref-241\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-241\">[241]</a></sup> However, on December 17, 2013, he suffered a broken bone in his knee, and did not return for the remainder of the season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-242\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-242\">[242]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-243\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-243\">[243]</a></sup> On March 25, 2014, the Lakers scored 51 points in the third quarter against the New York Knicks, the most points scored in a quarter in the history of the franchise.<sup id=\"cite_ref-244\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-244\">[244]</a></sup> The Lakers went on to miss the NBA playoffs for the first time since 2005, for just the second time in the last two decades and for just the sixth time in franchise history. On April 30, 2014, Mike D'Antoni resigned from his position as head coach after a 27&ndash;55 season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-245\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-245\">[245]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>After spending the majority of the off-season without a head coach, the Lakers named former player <a title=\"Byron Scott\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byron_Scott\">Byron Scott</a> as the new head coach.<sup id=\"cite_ref-246\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-246\">[246]</a></sup> After the season, he was the frontrunner to become the new Lakers head coach. Scott interviewed three times for the position, which had become vacant after <a title=\"Mike D'Antoni\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_D%27Antoni\">Mike D'Antoni</a>'s resignation.<sup id=\"cite_ref-247\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-247\">[247]</a></sup> On July 28, 2014, he signed a multi-year contract to coach the Lakers.<sup id=\"cite_ref-248\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-248\">[248]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>During the first game of the <a title=\"2014&ndash;15 Los Angeles Lakers season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Los_Angeles_Lakers_season\">2014&ndash;15</a> season, the seventh overall pick in the <a title=\"2014 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_NBA_draft\">2014 NBA draft</a>, <a title=\"Julius Randle\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julius_Randle\">Julius Randle</a> went down with a broken leg, which ended his rookie season. The Lakers began their season losing 10 of their first 16 games. After playing only 35 games, Kobe Bryant tore a rotator cuff in his shoulder ending his season. <a title=\"Nick Young (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nick_Young_(basketball)\">Nick Young</a> was also forced to end his season with a fractured kneecap, leaving the team with a record of 14&ndash;41.<sup id=\"cite_ref-249\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-249\">[249]</a></sup> With 27 games left in the regular season, Byron Scott gave rookie <a title=\"Jordan Clarkson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan_Clarkson\">Jordan Clarkson</a> more playing time. Clarkson, the 46th overall pick in the 2014 draft, finished his rookie season with game stats of 11.9 ppg, 3.2 rpg, 3.5 apg, and shooting 44.8% from the field.<sup id=\"cite_ref-250\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-250\">[250]</a></sup> The Lakers' season ended with a record of 21&ndash;61, the fourth worst record in the league and at the time the worst record in franchise history.</p>\r\n<p>The next season, the Lakers had the second overall pick of the <a title=\"2015 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_NBA_draft\">2015 NBA draft</a>, which they used to select <a title=\"Ohio State Buckeyes men's basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ohio_State_Buckeyes_men%27s_basketball\">Ohio State</a> freshman point guard <a title=\"D'Angelo Russell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D%27Angelo_Russell\">D'Angelo Russell</a>. The team also selected <a title=\"Larry Nance Jr.\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larry_Nance_Jr.\">Larry Nance Jr.</a> with the 27th overall pick.<sup id=\"cite_ref-autogenerated1_251-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-autogenerated1-251\">[251]</a></sup> On November 30, 2015, Bryant announced he would retire at the end of the season after 20 seasons with the team.<sup id=\"cite_ref-252\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-252\">[252]</a></sup> In Bryant's last season the team missed the playoffs for the third straight year with a 17&ndash;65 record, the worst in franchise history.<sup id=\"cite_ref-253\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-253\">[253]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"2016.E2.80.932018:_Post-Bryant_era\"></span><span id=\"2016&ndash;2018:_Post-Bryant_era\" class=\"mw-headline\">2016&ndash;2018: Post-Bryant era</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Frank_Vogel_NBA_TV_(cropped).jpeg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Frank_Vogel_NBA_TV_%28cropped%29.jpeg/170px-Frank_Vogel_NBA_TV_%28cropped%29.jpeg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Frank_Vogel_NBA_TV_%28cropped%29.jpeg/255px-Frank_Vogel_NBA_TV_%28cropped%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Frank_Vogel_NBA_TV_%28cropped%29.jpeg/340px-Frank_Vogel_NBA_TV_%28cropped%29.jpeg 2x\" width=\"170\" height=\"230\" data-file-width=\"1904\" data-file-height=\"2580\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Frank Vogel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Vogel\">Frank Vogel</a>, who coached the Lakers for three seasons</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>On April 24, 2016, the Lakers announced that they would not exercise their option on Byron Scott's contract for the following season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-254\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-254\">[254]</a></sup> On April 29, the team announced another former Laker, <a title=\"Luke Walton\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luke_Walton\">Luke Walton</a>, as their new head coach. At the time of his hiring, Walton was an assistant coach for the <a title=\"Golden State Warriors\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors\">Golden State Warriors</a>, who were in the <a title=\"2016 NBA playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_NBA_playoffs\">playoffs</a>, so he could not officially begin his duties as head coach until the Warriors' playoff run was over.<sup id=\"cite_ref-255\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-255\">[255]</a></sup> The Lakers earned the second overall pick in the <a title=\"2016 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_NBA_draft\">2016 NBA draft</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-256\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-256\">[256]</a></sup> and selected <a title=\"Brandon Ingram\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brandon_Ingram\">Brandon Ingram</a> from <a title=\"Duke Blue Devils men's basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duke_Blue_Devils_men%27s_basketball\">Duke University</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-257\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-257\">[257]</a></sup> The team also selected <a title=\"Ivica Zubac\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivica_Zubac\">Ivica Zubac</a> with the 32nd overall pick.<sup id=\"cite_ref-258\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-258\">[258]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>On February 21, 2017, the Lakers fired general manager Mitch Kupchak, while <a title=\"Magic Johnson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magic_Johnson\">Magic Johnson</a> was named as the president of basketball operations. The team's governor Jeanie Buss, also announced the removal of her brother, <a title=\"Jim Buss\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Buss\">Jim Buss</a>, from his position as executive vice president of basketball operations.<sup id=\"cite_ref-2017LakersJohnson_259-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-2017LakersJohnson-259\">[259]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-260\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-260\">[260]</a></sup> On March 7, 2017, the Lakers hired <a title=\"Rob Pelinka\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rob_Pelinka\">Rob Pelinka</a> as the general manager, signing him to a five-year deal.<sup id=\"cite_ref-261\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-261\">[261]</a></sup> The Lakers again earned the second overall pick, this time, in the <a title=\"2017 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_NBA_draft\">2017 NBA draft</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-262\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-262\">[262]</a></sup> and selected <a title=\"Lonzo Ball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lonzo_Ball\">Lonzo Ball</a> from <a title=\"UCLA Bruins men's basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UCLA_Bruins_men%27s_basketball\">UCLA</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-263\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-263\">[263]</a></sup> The Lakers also acquired <a title=\"Kyle Kuzma\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyle_Kuzma\">Kyle Kuzma</a> from the <a title=\"Utah Utes men's basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utah_Utes_men%27s_basketball\">University of Utah</a> with the 27th overall pick from a draft-day trade, along with <a title=\"Brook Lopez\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brook_Lopez\">Brook Lopez</a> in exchange for <a title=\"D'Angelo Russell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D%27Angelo_Russell\">D'Angelo Russell</a> and <a title=\"Timofey Mozgov\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timofey_Mozgov\">Timofey Mozgov</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-264\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-264\">[264]</a></sup> The Lakers also traded their 28th overall pick, <a title=\"Tony Bradley (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Bradley_(basketball)\">Tony Bradley</a>, in exchange for the 30th overall pick, <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Josh Hart (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josh_Hart_(basketball)\">Josh Hart</a>, from <a title=\"Villanova Wildcats men's basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Villanova_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball\">Villanova University</a> and the 42nd overall pick, <a title=\"Thomas Bryant (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Bryant_(basketball)\">Thomas Bryant</a>, from <a title=\"Indiana Hoosiers men's basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indiana_Hoosiers_men%27s_basketball\">Indiana University</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-265\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-265\">[265]</a></sup> In February 2018, Nance Jr. and Clarkson were traded away to the <a title=\"Cleveland Cavaliers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cleveland_Cavaliers\">Cleveland Cavaliers</a> in exchange for <a title=\"Isaiah Thomas (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaiah_Thomas_(basketball)\">Isaiah Thomas</a>, <a title=\"Channing Frye\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Channing_Frye\">Channing Frye</a>, and a 2018
