first-round draft pick.<sup id=\"cite_ref-266\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-266\">[266]</a></sup> On July 2, 2018, Randle was renounced by the Lakers.<sup id=\"cite_ref-267\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-267\">[267]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"2018.E2.80.93present:_The_LeBron_James_era\"></span><span id=\"2018&ndash;present:_The_LeBron_James_era\" class=\"mw-headline\">2018&ndash;present: The LeBron James era</span></h3>\r\n<h4><span id=\"2018.E2.80.932019:_The_arrival_of_LeBron_James\"></span><span id=\"2018&ndash;2019:_The_arrival_of_LeBron_James\" class=\"mw-headline\">2018&ndash;2019: The arrival of LeBron James</span></h4>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 182px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:LeBron_James_Lakers.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/LeBron_James_Lakers.jpg/180px-LeBron_James_Lakers.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/LeBron_James_Lakers.jpg/270px-LeBron_James_Lakers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/LeBron_James_Lakers.jpg/360px-LeBron_James_Lakers.jpg 2x\" width=\"180\" height=\"295\" data-file-width=\"661\" data-file-height=\"1084\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 182px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"LeBron James\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LeBron_James\">LeBron James</a> in 2018</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>On July 9, 2018, the Lakers signed <a title=\"LeBron James\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LeBron_James\">LeBron James</a> to a four-year, $154&nbsp;million contract.<sup id=\"cite_ref-268\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-268\">[268]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-269\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-269\">[269]</a></sup> By the Christmas Day game, the Lakers were six games over .500 before James sustained a groin injury leading to several weeks of missed games. Ball and Ingram also ended their seasons early due to injuries. On February 7, 2019, Zubac was traded to the Los Angeles Clippers along with <a title=\"Michael Beasley\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Beasley\">Michael Beasley</a> in exchange for <a title=\"Mike Muscala\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Muscala\">Mike Muscala</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-270\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-270\">[270]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>On April 9, 2019, Johnson stepped down as the team's president of basketball operations,<sup id=\"cite_ref-271\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-271\">[271]</a></sup> and two days later, the Lakers parted ways with head coach Walton after the team failed to reach the playoffs for the sixth straight year.<sup id=\"cite_ref-272\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-272\">[272]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h4><span id=\"2019.E2.80.93present:_James_and_Davis_era\"></span><span id=\"2019&ndash;present:_James_and_Davis_era\" class=\"mw-headline\">2019&ndash;present: James and Davis era</span></h4>\r\n<p>On May 13, <a title=\"Frank Vogel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Vogel\">Frank Vogel</a> was named the Lakers' head coach.<sup id=\"cite_ref-273\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-273\">[273]</a></sup> The Lakers received the fourth overall pick in the <a title=\"2019 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_NBA_draft\">2019 NBA draft lottery</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-274\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-274\">[274]</a></sup> On July 6, the Lakers acquired <a title=\"Anthony Davis\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthony_Davis\">Anthony Davis</a> from the <a title=\"New Orleans Pelicans\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Orleans_Pelicans\">New Orleans Pelicans</a> for Ball, Ingram, Hart, and three first-round picks, including the number four overall in the 2019 draft.<sup id=\"cite_ref-275\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-275\">[275]</a></sup> This trade officially ended the young core era of the Lakers; only Kuzma remained out of the group of players.</p>\r\n<p>Following the <a title=\"Suspension of the 2019&ndash;20 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suspension_of_the_2019%E2%80%9320_NBA_season\">suspension of the 2019&ndash;20 NBA season</a>, the Lakers were one of the 22 teams invited to the <a title=\"2020 NBA Bubble\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_NBA_Bubble\">NBA Bubble</a> to participate in the final eight games of the regular season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-276\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-276\">[276]</a></sup> The Lakers finished the regular season with a 52&ndash;19 record, entering the playoffs for the first time since 2013,<sup id=\"cite_ref-277\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-277\">[277]</a></sup> and as the top seed for the first time since 2010.<sup id=\"cite_ref-278\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-278\">[278]</a></sup> They advanced to the NBA Finals for the first time since 2010.<sup id=\"cite_ref-279\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-279\">[279]</a></sup> They defeated the <a title=\"Miami Heat\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miami_Heat\">Miami Heat</a> 4&ndash;2 to win the <a title=\"2020 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_NBA_Finals\">2020 NBA Finals</a>,<sup id=\"cite_ref-280\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-280\">[280]</a></sup> and James was named the Finals MVP for the fourth time in his career.<sup id=\"cite_ref-281\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-281\">[281]</a></sup> The win gave Los Angeles their 17th championship in franchise history, tying the Boston Celtics for the most all-time.<sup id=\"cite_ref-mcmenamin_10112020_282-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-mcmenamin_10112020-282\">[282]</a></sup> Primary Lakers owner <a title=\"Jeanie Buss\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeanie_Buss\">Jeanie Buss</a>, who took over the team in 2017, would also become the first female controlling owner of an NBA team to win the NBA Finals.<sup id=\"cite_ref-283\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-283\">[283]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>During the 2021 off-season, the Lakers picked up many NBA veterans, the most notable of which was <a title=\"Russell Westbrook\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russell_Westbrook\">Russell Westbrook</a>, who was acquired in a blockbuster trade with the <a title=\"Washington Wizards\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_Wizards\">Washington Wizards</a>. <a title=\"Kyle Kuzma\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyle_Kuzma\">Kyle Kuzma</a>, the last player left from the Lakers' young core era, was traded away, along with others. Other veterans picked up during the off-season included <a title=\"Carmelo Anthony\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carmelo_Anthony\">Carmelo Anthony</a>, <a title=\"DeAndre Jordan\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DeAndre_Jordan\">DeAndre Jordan</a>, and returning players <a title=\"Wayne Ellington\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Ellington\">Wayne Ellington</a>, <a title=\"Trevor Ariza\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trevor_Ariza\">Trevor Ariza</a>, <a title=\"Dwight Howard\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwight_Howard\">Dwight Howard</a> and <a title=\"Rajon Rondo\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rajon_Rondo\">Rajon Rondo</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-284\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-284\">[284]</a></sup> <a title=\"Alex Caruso\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alex_Caruso\">Alex Caruso</a> left the Lakers and signed with the <a title=\"Chicago Bulls\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago_Bulls\">Chicago Bulls</a>, and veteran locker-room voice <a title=\"Jared Dudley\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jared_Dudley\">Jared Dudley</a> retired.<sup id=\"cite_ref-285\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-285\">[285]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-286\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-286\">[286]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Rivalries\" class=\"mw-headline\">Rivalries</span></h2>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Boston_Celtics\" class=\"mw-headline\">Boston Celtics</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"Celtics&ndash;Lakers rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celtics%E2%80%93Lakers_rivalry\">Celtics&ndash;Lakers rivalry</a></div>\r\n<p>The rivalry between the <a title=\"Boston Celtics\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_Celtics\">Boston Celtics</a> and the Lakers involves the two most storied <a title=\"Basketball\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basketball\">basketball</a> franchises in <a title=\"National Basketball Association\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_Association\">National Basketball Association</a> (NBA) history. It has been called the best rivalry in the NBA.<sup id=\"cite_ref-287\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-287\">[287]</a></sup> The two teams have met a record 12 times in the <a title=\"NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a>, starting with their first Finals meeting in <a title=\"1959 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1959_NBA_Finals\">1959</a>. They would go on to dominate the league in the 1960s and the 1980s, facing each other six times in the 1960s and three times in the 1980s.</p>\r\n<p>The rivalry had been less intense since the retirements of <a title=\"Magic Johnson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magic_Johnson\">Magic Johnson</a> and <a title=\"Larry Bird\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larry_Bird\">Larry Bird</a> in the early 1990s, but in 2008 it was renewed as the Celtics and Lakers met in the Finals for the first time since 1987, with the Celtics winning the series 4&ndash;2. They faced off once again in the <a title=\"2010 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_NBA_Finals\">2010 NBA Finals</a>, which the Lakers won in 7 games.</p>\r\n<p>The two teams have tied for the highest number of championships, with 17 titles apiece; together, the 34 championships account for almost half of the <a title=\"List of NBA champions\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_NBA_champions\">74 championships</a> in NBA history.</p>\r\n<p>The all-time series record for the Lakers vs Celtics is 204&ndash;162 with the Celtics being the forerunners.<sup id=\"cite_ref-288\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-288\">[288]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Detroit_Pistons\" class=\"mw-headline\">Detroit Pistons</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"Lakers&ndash;Pistons rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lakers%E2%80%93Pistons_rivalry\">Lakers&ndash;Pistons rivalry</a></div>\r\n<p>The rivalry between the Lakers and the <a title=\"Detroit Pistons\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Detroit_Pistons\">Detroit Pistons</a> developed in the late 1980s.<sup id=\"cite_ref-289\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-289\">[289]</a></sup><sup class=\"reference nowrap\"><span title=\"Page / location: 228\">: 228 </span></sup> Both teams faced each other in back-to-back finals appearances in the <a title=\"1988 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988_NBA_Finals\">1988 NBA Finals</a>, which the Lakers won in 7 games and the <a title=\"1989 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989_NBA_Finals\">1989 NBA Finals</a>, which the Pistons won in 4 games.</p>\r\n<p>The rivalry reemerged in the early 2000s as both teams squared off against one another in the <a title=\"2004 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_NBA_Finals\">2004 NBA Finals</a>, which the Pistons won in five games.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Golden_State_Warriors\" class=\"mw-headline\">Golden State Warriors</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"Lakers&ndash;Warriors rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lakers%E2%80%93Warriors_rivalry\">Lakers&ndash;Warriors rivalry</a></div>\r\n<p>The Lakers have a lengthy history with the <a title=\"Golden State Warriors\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors\">Golden State Warriors</a> as both franchises relocated to California during the early 1960s. Geography does play a minor role in the rivalry; however there exists more respect between both teams and fans alike. Unlike the <a title=\"Dodgers&ndash;Giants rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dodgers%E2%80%93Giants_rivalry\">Dodgers&ndash;Giants rivalry</a> of MLB, or the <a title=\"49ers&ndash;Rams rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/49ers%E2%80%93Rams_rivalry\">49ers&ndash;Rams rivalry</a> of the NFL in which both teams express fierce animosity against one another.<sup id=\"cite_ref-290\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-290\">[290]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-291\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-291\">[291]</a></sup> The rivalry began to sprout during the 1970s as the two teams would meet six times in the postseason from 1967 to 1991. Both teams fluctuated in success at varying times, however; the Lakers recent rise following the signing of <a title=\"LeBron James\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LeBron_James\">LeBron James</a> contributed heavily to adding a level of competition between both sides as James had previously faced the Warriors in four straight finals as a member of the Cavaliers. Both teams have met seven times in the postseason, combining for 38 division titles since both teams relocated to California in the early 1960s.<sup id=\"cite_ref-292\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-292\">[292]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-293\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-293\">[293]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-294\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-294\">[294]</a></sup> The Lakers lead the all time regular season series 262&ndash;173, and the postseason series 25&ndash;11.<sup id=\"cite_ref-295\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-295\">[295]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-296\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-296\">[296]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Los_Angeles_Clippers\" class=\"mw-headline\">Los Angeles Clippers</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"Lakers&ndash;Clippers rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lakers%E2%80%93Clippers_rivalry\">Lakers&ndash;Clippers rivalry</a></div>\r\n<p>The rivalry between the Lakers and the <a title=\"Los Angeles Clippers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Clippers\">Los Angeles Clippers</a> is unique because they are the only two NBA teams to share an arena, the <a title=\"Crypto.com Arena\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crypto.com_Arena\">Crypto.com Arena</a>. It is also one of only two intra-city rivalries in the NBA, the other being the new crosstown rivalry between the <a title=\"New York Knicks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Knicks\">New York Knicks</a> and <a title=\"Brooklyn Nets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets\">Brooklyn Nets</a>.</p>\r\n<p>Los Angeles fans have historically favored the Lakers.<sup id=\"cite_ref-gold_297-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-gold-297\">[297]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-298\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-298\">[298]</a></sup> Some contend that the term <em>rivalry</em> was inaccurate until the Clippers became more successful.<sup id=\"cite_ref-299\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-299\">[299]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"San_Antonio_Spurs\" class=\"mw-headline\">San Antonio Spurs</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"Lakers&ndash;Spurs rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lakers%E2%80%93Spurs_rivalry\">Lakers&ndash;Spurs rivalry</a></div>\r\n<p>The <a title=\"San Antonio Spurs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Antonio_Spurs\">San Antonio Spurs</a> and the Lakers, developed what some would classify as a rivalry in the late 1990s and early 2000s. Since 1999, the teams have met in the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"NBA Playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Playoffs\">NBA Playoffs</a> five times, with the clubs combining to appear in seven consecutive <a title=\"NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Finals\">NBA Finals</a> (from 1999 to 2005). Additionally, the teams combined to win five NBA championships from 1999 to 2003; the Spurs won the NBA championship in 1999, 2003, 2005, 2007 and 2014 while the Lakers won the championship in 2000, 2001, 2002, 2009 and 2010. From 1999 to 2004 the clubs' rivalry was often considered the premier rivalry in the NBA,<sup id=\"cite_ref-300\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-300\">[300]</a></sup> and each time the clubs faced each other in the playoffs the winner advanced to the NBA Finals. In 2008, the teams met again in the Western Conference Finals where the Spurs were handily defeated only to beat the Lakers when they met again in 2013.</p>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Sacramento_Kings\" class=\"mw-headline\">Sacramento Kings</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"Kings-Lakers rivalry\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kings-Lakers_rivalry\">Kings-Lakers rivalry</a></div>\r\n<p>The Kings and the Lakers have faced each other in the playoffs nine times between 1949 and 2002, and since the Kings moved to Sacramento in 1985, both have been based in California. The <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"2002 NBA Playoffs\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_NBA_Playoffs#Western_Conference_finals\">2002 Western Conference Finals</a> was one of the most bitterly contested in NBA history, with many controversial calls in game 6. <sup id=\"cite_ref-301\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-301\">[301]</a></sup> The Lakers would win the series in game 7.</p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Ownerships.2C_financial_history.2C_and_fanbase\"></span><span id=\"Ownerships,_financial_history,_and_fanbase\" class=\"mw-headline\">Ownerships, financial history, and fanbase</span></h2>\r\n<p>Berger and Chalfen purchased the NBL's disbanded Detroit Gems for $15,000 in 1947, changed their name to the Lakers, and relocated them to Minnesota. Max Winter bought a third of the club in their early years and sold his share to Mikan in 1954. Berger bought Mikan's share in 1956 giving him a controlling (⅔) interest.<sup id=\"cite_ref-dirt_302-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-dirt-302\">[302]</a></sup> After Mikan retired, attendance plummeted and the team lost money for several seasons, leading the ownership group to put the team up for sale in 1957.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Sara_303-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Sara-303\">[303]</a></sup> <a title=\"Marty Marion\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marty_Marion\">Marty Marion</a>, a retired baseball player and manager, and his business partner Milton Fischman attempted to purchase the team with the intention of moving the club to <a title=\"Kansas City, Missouri\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kansas_City,_Missouri\">Kansas City, Missouri</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Sara_303-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Sara-303\">[303]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-Minn_304-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Minn-304\">[304]</a></sup> Mikan offered to mortgage his home in an attempt to buy the team and keep the club in Minnesota.<sup id=\"cite_ref-305\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-305\">[305]</a></sup> The Lakers were sold to a group of investors led by Bob Short, however.<sup id=\"cite_ref-dirt_302-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-dirt-302\">[302]</a></sup> The team was sold to Short's group with the agreement that it would not be relocated to Kansas City but kept in Minnesota.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Mil_306-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Mil-306\">[306]</a></sup> Short's ownership group consisted of 117 Minnesota businesses and private citizens, who amassed a total of $200,000 for the purchase; $150,000 to buy the team and $50,000 to run it.<sup id=\"cite_ref-dirt_302-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-dirt-302\">[302]</a></sup> By 1958 Short had become 80% owner of the team by buying out his partners,<sup id=\"cite_ref-dirt_302-3\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-dirt-302\">[302]</a></sup> but the team was floundering. Attendance remained poor, and the NBA had put the Lakers on \"financial probation\", notifying them that if they did not meet certain ticket sales numbers they could be bought out by the league and relocated. Short was forced to move the team to Los Angeles in 1960; the club had lost $60,000 in the first half of the 1959&ndash;60 season alone.<sup id=\"cite_ref-307\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-307\">[307]</a></sup> The NBA's owners originally voted 7&ndash;1 against the move.<sup id=\"cite_ref-308\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-308\">[308]</a></sup> When Short indicated that he might take the team to a new rival league that was developing, however, the owners held another vote that same day and allowed the relocation (8&ndash;0).<sup id=\"cite_ref-309\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-309\">[309]</a></sup> Aided by Baylor's drawing power,<sup id=\"cite_ref-310\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-310\">[310]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-311\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-311\">[311]</a></sup> and the new locale, the team's finances improved when they arrived in LA.<sup id=\"cite_ref-312\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-312\">[312]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-313\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-313\">[313]</a></sup> Short sold the team to <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Washington Redskins\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_Redskins\">Washington Redskins</a> owner and publisher Jack Kent Cooke in 1965 for a then league record amount of $5.175&nbsp;million.<sup id=\"cite_ref-314\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-314\">[314]</a></sup> Short insisted the deal be conducted in cash as he was wary of Cooke, so guards transported the money in a cart from one New York bank to another.<sup id=\"cite_ref-315\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-315\">[315]</a></sup></p>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tleft\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jerry_Buss_playing_the_WSOP.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Jerry_Buss_playing_the_WSOP.jpg/170px-Jerry_Buss_playing_the_WSOP.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Jerry_Buss_playing_the_WSOP.jpg/255px-Jerry_Buss_playing_the_WSOP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Jerry_Buss_playing_the_WSOP.jpg/340px-Jerry_Buss_playing_the_WSOP.jpg 2x\" width=\"170\" height=\"254\" data-file-width=\"1285\" data-file-height=\"1920\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tleft\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a title=\"Jerry Buss\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerry_Buss\">Jerry Buss</a> owned the team from 1979 until his death in 2013.</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>Cooke was a more hands-on owner than Short, and overhauled the team's operations.<sup id=\"cite_ref-316\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-316\">[316]</a></sup> He personally financed construction of the Forum in 1967 at a cost of $16.5&nbsp;million.<sup id=\"cite_ref-317\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-317\">[317]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-Star_318-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Star-318\">[318]</a></sup> He owned the team until 1979 when he sold it, the NHL's Los Angeles Kings, the Forum, and some real estate to <a title=\"Jerry Buss\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerry_Buss\">Jerry Buss</a> for $67&nbsp;million.<sup id=\"cite_ref-319\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-319\">[319]</a></sup> Cooke was forced to sell the team as he was undergoing a costly divorce.<sup id=\"cite_ref-320\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-320\">[320]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-321\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-321\">[321]</a></sup> Buss was a local chemical engineer and former <a title=\"University of Southern California\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Southern_California\">University of Southern California</a> professor who had become wealthy in real estate.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Star_318-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Star-318\">[318]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-322\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-322\">[322]</a></sup> <a title=\"Philip Anschutz\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_Anschutz\">Philip Anschutz</a> bought a stake in the team in 1998,<sup id=\"cite_ref-FB2009_323-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-FB2009-323\">[323]</a></sup> and until October 2010 Magic Johnson was a minority owner as well.<sup id=\"cite_ref-324\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-324\">[324]</a></sup> Buss started the trend of allowing sponsors to add their name to team's stadiums when he renamed the Forum the <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Great Western Bank (1919&ndash;97)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Western_Bank_(1919%E2%80%9397)\">Great Western</a> Forum in 1988.<sup id=\"cite_ref-325\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-325\">[325]</a></sup> In 2009 major sponsors included <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Verizon Wireless\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Verizon_Wireless\">Verizon Wireless</a>, <a title=\"Toyota\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toyota\">Toyota</a>, <a title=\"Anheuser-Busch\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anheuser-Busch\">Anheuser-Busch</a>, <a title=\"American Express\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Express\">American Express</a>, and <a title=\"Carl's Jr.\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl%27s_Jr.\">Carl's Jr.</a>, and the team's $113 average ticket price was the highest in the league.<sup id=\"cite_ref-FB2009_323-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-FB2009-323\">[323]</a></sup> In 2013, Buss died at the age of 80 after being hospitalized for 18 months with cancer.<sup id=\"cite_ref-326\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-326\">[326]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-327\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-327\">[327]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-328\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-328\">[328]</a></sup> His controlling ownership of the team passed to his six children via a trust, with each child receiving an equal vote.<sup id=\"cite_ref-329\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-329\">[329]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-markazi_02182013_330-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-markazi_02182013-330\">[330]</a></sup> Buss' succession plan had daughter <a title=\"Jeanie Buss\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeanie_Buss\">Jeanie Buss</a> assume his title as the Lakers' governor as well as its team representative at NBA Board of Governors meetings.<sup id=\"cite_ref-markazi_02182013_330-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-markazi_02182013-330\">[330]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-bresnahan_02192013_331-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-bresnahan_02192013-331\">[331]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Given the team's proximity to Hollywood, the Lakers fanbase includes numerous celebrities, many of whom can be seen at the Staples Center during home games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-332\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-332\">[332]</a></sup> <a title=\"Jack Nicholson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jack_Nicholson\">Jack Nicholson</a>, for example, has held season tickets since the 1970s, and directors reportedly need to work their shooting schedules around Lakers home games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-celfans_333-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-celfans-333\">[333]</a></sup> From 2002 and 2007 the team averaged just over 18,900 fans, which placed them in the top ten in the NBA in attendance. <a title=\"Red Hot Chili Peppers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Hot_Chili_Peppers\">Red Hot Chili Peppers</a>' song \"Magic Johnson\", from their 1989 album <em><a title=\"Mother's Milk (album)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mother%27s_Milk_(album)\">Mother's Milk</a></em>, is a tribute to the former point guard, and frontman <a title=\"Anthony Kiedis\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthony_Kiedis\">Anthony Kiedis</a> and bassist <a title=\"Flea (musician)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flea_(musician)\">Michael \"Flea\" Balzary</a> are frequently seen attending home games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-334\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-334\">[334]</a></sup> In 2008, the team sold out every home game,<sup id=\"cite_ref-335\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-335\">[335]</a></sup> and in 2010, the Lakers had the most popular team merchandise among all NBA teams, and Bryant the most popular jersey.<sup id=\"cite_ref-336\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-336\">[336]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Name.2C_logo.2C_and_uniforms\"></span><span id=\"Name,_logo,_and_uniforms\" class=\"mw-headline\">Name, logo, and uniforms</span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Further information: <a title=\"Logos and uniforms of the Los Angeles Lakers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logos_and_uniforms_of_the_Los_Angeles_Lakers\">Logos and uniforms of the Los Angeles Lakers</a></div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Los_Angeles_Lakers_Wordmark_Logo_2001-current.svg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Los_Angeles_Lakers_Wordmark_Logo_2001-current.svg/170px-Los_Angeles_Lakers_Wordmark_Logo_2001-current.svg.png\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Los_Angeles_Lakers_Wordmark_Logo_2001-current.svg/255px-Los_Angeles_Lakers_Wordmark_Logo_2001-current.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Los_Angeles_Lakers_Wordmark_Logo_2001-current.svg/340px-Los_Angeles_Lakers_Wordmark_Logo_2001-current.svg.png 2x\" width=\"170\" height=\"57\" data-file-width=\"329\" data-file-height=\"110\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">The Lakers current wordmark, used since the 1999&ndash;2000 season. The version shown is used on their \"Association\" white jerseys.</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>The Laker nickname came from the state of Minnesota being the <em>Land of 10,000 Lakes</em>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-The_Nicknames_11-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-The_Nicknames-11\">[11]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-337\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-337\">[337]</a></sup> The team's colors are purple, gold and white.<sup id=\"cite_ref-GoingRetroLakers_338-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-GoingRetroLakers-338\">[338]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-LakersLogosheet_6-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LakersLogosheet-6\">[6]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-339\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-339\">[339]</a></sup> The Lakers logo consists of the team name, \"Los Angeles Lakers\" written in purple on top of a gold basketball. The team usually wears white jerseys for Sunday and holiday home games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-GoingRetroLakers_338-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-GoingRetroLakers-338\">[338]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-340\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-340\">[340]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Season-by-season_record\" class=\"mw-headline\">Season-by-season record</span></h2>\r\n<p><em>List of the last five seasons completed by the Lakers. For the full season-by-season history, see <a title=\"List of Los Angeles Lakers seasons\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Los_Angeles_Lakers_seasons\">List of Los Angeles Lakers seasons</a>.</em></p>\r\n<p>The Lakers have won 17 NBA titles and have appeared in the NBA Finals 15 other times.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL_32-7\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL-32\">[32]</a></sup> These appearances include eight NBA Finals appearances in the 1980s. The best record posted by the team was 69&ndash;13, in 1972; the worst record was 17&ndash;65, in 2016.<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL_32-8\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL-32\">[32]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p><em><strong>Note:</strong> GP = Games played, W = Wins, L = Losses, W&ndash;L% = Winning percentage</em></p>\r\n<table class=\"wikitable\">\r\n<tbody>\r\n<tr style=\"font-weight: bold; background-color: #552583; color: Conference Finals, 0&ndash;4 (<a title=\"Denver Nuggets\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denver_Nuggets\">Nuggets</a>)</td>\r\n</tr>\r\n</tbody>\r\n</table>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Franchise_and_NBA_records\" class=\"mw-headline\">Franchise and NBA records</span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Further information: <a title=\"Los Angeles Lakers accomplishments and records\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers_accomplishments_and_records\">Los Angeles Lakers accomplishments and records</a></div>\r\n<p>Bryant holds most individual team records for longevity including most games played (1,333), and most minutes logged (48,298). Johnson holds all significant assist records for the club including career assists (10,141), assists in a game (24), and highest assist average for a season (13.1). Johnson also has the most <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Triple double\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Triple_double\">triple doubles</a>, with his 138 over 100 more than the next closest player (Bryant; 17). <a title=\"Elmore Smith\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elmore_Smith\">Elmore Smith</a> holds team records for blocks in a game (17), blocks per game for a season (4.85), and career blocks per game (3.93). The scoring records are mostly shared by <a title=\"Elgin Baylor\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elgin_Baylor\">Elgin Baylor</a> and Bryant, with Baylor having the highest average for a career (27.4) while Bryant has the highest points scored in a single game (81). Baylor, Bryant and West hold the top five single-season scoring averages, with Bryant occupying the first (35.4) and fourth (31.6) spots, while Baylor has the second (34.8), and third (34.0), and West the fifth (31.3).<sup id=\"cite_ref-341\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-341\">[341]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-342\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-342\">[342]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>The Lakers hold several NBA records as a team including most consecutive games won overall (33) and most consecutive road games won (16), both of which came during the 1971&ndash;72 season,<sup id=\"cite_ref-teamrec_343-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-teamrec-343\">[343]</a></sup> highest field-goal percentage for a season at 54.5% (1984&ndash;85),<sup id=\"cite_ref-344\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-344\">[344]</a></sup> and highest road winning percentage at 0.816 (1971&ndash;72).<sup id=\"cite_ref-nba10_61-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-nba10-61\">[61]</a></sup> They also hold records for having (into the <a title=\"2009&ndash;10 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_NBA_season\">2009&ndash;10 season</a>) the most wins (3,027), the highest winning percentage (61.9%), and the most NBA Finals appearances (31).<sup id=\"cite_ref-LAL_32-9\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-LAL-32\">[32]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-team_345-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-team-345\">[345]</a></sup> The 2000&ndash;01 team set the NBA record for best playoff record at 15&ndash;1, which was later broken by the <a title=\"Golden State Warriors\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors\">Golden State Warriors</a> in 2017.<sup id=\"cite_ref-2017PlayoffsRecord_346-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-2017PlayoffsRecord-346\">[346]</a></sup> The 1971&ndash;72 team holds franchise records in wins (69), most points scored, and largest margin of victory; both of the latter came in the team's 63 point win versus Golden State (162&ndash;99).<sup id=\"cite_ref-347\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-347\">[347]</a></sup> They also held the record for most wins at home in the regular season (going 36&ndash;5 in 1971&ndash;72, then 37&ndash;4 in both 1976&ndash;77 and 1979&ndash;80) unil the Boston Celtics set the current record of 40&ndash;1 in the 1985&ndash;86 season.</p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Home_arenas\" class=\"mw-headline\">Home arenas</span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tmulti tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner multiimageinner\" style=\"width: 492px; max-width: 492px;\">\r\n<div class=\"trow\">\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 251px; max-width: 251px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 163px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:GreatWesternForum.jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/GreatWesternForum.jpg/249px-GreatWesternForum.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/GreatWesternForum.jpg/374px-GreatWesternForum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/GreatWesternForum.jpg/498px-GreatWesternForum.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"249\" height=\"164\" data-file-width=\"3800\" data-file-height=\"2500\"></a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"tsingle\" style=\"width: 237px; max-width: 237px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbimage\" style=\"height: 163px; overflow: hidden;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Staples_Center,_LA,_CA,_jjron_22.03.2012.jpg\"><img src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Staples_Center%2C_LA%2C_CA%2C_jjron_22.03.2012.jpg/235px-Staples_Center%2C_LA%2C_CA%2C_jjron_22.03.2012.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Staples_Center%2C_LA%2C_CA%2C_jjron_22.03.2012.jpg/353px-Staples_Center%2C_LA%2C_CA%2C_jjron_22.03.2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Staples_Center%2C_LA%2C_CA%2C_jjron_22.03.2012.jpg/470px-Staples_Center%2C_LA%2C_CA%2C_jjron_22.03.2012.jpg 2x\" alt=\"\" width=\"235\" height=\"164\" data-file-width=\"3203\" data-file-height=\"2233\"></a></div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"trow\" style=\"display: flex;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\"><a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"The Forum (Inglewood, California)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Forum_(Inglewood,_California)\">The Forum</a> (left), served as the Lakers' home arena from 1967 to 1999, before they moved to their present home, the <a title=\"Crypto.com Arena\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crypto.com_Arena\">Crypto.com Arena</a> (right).</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<p>The Lakers play their home games at <a title=\"Crypto.com Arena\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crypto.com_Arena\">Crypto.com Arena</a>, located at <a title=\"L.A. Live\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/L.A._Live\">L.A. Live</a> in <a title=\"Downtown Los Angeles\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Downtown_Los_Angeles\">Downtown Los Angeles</a>. The arena opened in fall 1999 and seats up to 18,997 for Lakers games.<sup id=\"cite_ref-About_STAPLES_Center_348-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-About_STAPLES_Center-348\">[348]</a></sup> Owned and operated by <a title=\"Anschutz Entertainment Group\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anschutz_Entertainment_Group\">AEG</a> and L.A. Arena Company, the arena is also home to the Los Angeles Clippers, the WNBA's Los Angeles Sparks, and the NHL's Los Angeles Kings.<sup id=\"cite_ref-About_STAPLES_Center_348-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-About_STAPLES_Center-348\">[348]</a></sup> Before moving to Staples Center, for 32 seasons (1967&ndash;1999), the Lakers played their home games at <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"The Forum (Inglewood, California)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Forum_(Inglewood,_California)\">The Forum</a> in <a title=\"Inglewood, California\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inglewood,_California\">Inglewood, California</a>, located approximately 10 miles southwest of the team's current home.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_#35_162-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_#35-162\">[162]</a></sup> During the 1999 preseason, the Lakers played their home games at the Forum before officially moving into Crypto.com Arena, and once again hosted a preseason game versus the <a title=\"Golden State Warriors\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors\">Golden State Warriors</a> on October 9, 2009, this time to commemorate the team's 50th anniversary season in Los Angeles.<sup id=\"cite_ref-349\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-349\">[349]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>In the first seven years in Los Angeles, the team played their home games at the <a title=\"Los Angeles Memorial Sports Arena\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Memorial_Sports_Arena\">Los Angeles Memorial Sports Arena</a>, south of Downtown Los Angeles.<sup id=\"cite_ref-350\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-350\">[350]</a></sup> While the team played in Minneapolis, the team played their home games at the <a title=\"Minneapolis Auditorium\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minneapolis_Auditorium\">Minneapolis Auditorium</a> from 1947 to 1960.<sup id=\"cite_ref-351\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-351\">[351]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Players\" class=\"mw-headline\">Players</span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">For the complete list of Los Angeles Lakers players, see <a title=\"Los Angeles Lakers all-time roster\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers_all-time_roster\">Los Angeles Lakers all-time roster</a>.</div>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Current_roster\" class=\"mw-headline\">Current roster</span></h3>\r\n<table class=\"toccolours\"><caption style=\"background-color: #552583; color: #ffffff; box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #FDB927, inset -2px -2px 0 #FDB927; ; text-align: class=\"mw-headline\">Retained draft rights</span></h3>\r\n<p>The Lakers hold the draft rights to the following unsigned draft picks who have been playing outside the NBA.<sup id=\"cite_ref-352\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-352\">[352]</a></sup> A drafted player, either an international draftee or a college draftee who is not signed by the team that drafted him, is allowed to sign with any non-NBA teams. In this case, the team retains the player's draft rights in the NBA until one year after the player's contract with the non-NBA team ends.<sup id=\"cite_ref-353\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-353\">[353]</a></sup> This list includes draft rights that were acquired from trades with other teams.</p>\r\n<table class=\"wikitable href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/VTB_United_League\">Russia</a>)</td>\r\n<td>Acquired from the <a title=\"New York Knicks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Knicks\">New York Knicks</a></td>\r\n<td><sup id=\"cite_ref-354\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-354\">[354]</a></sup></td>\r\n</tr>\r\n<tr>\r\n<td style=\"text-align: center;\"><a title=\"2009 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_NBA_draft\">2009</a></td>\r\n<td style=\"text-align: center;\">2</td>\r\n<td style=\"text-align: center;\">59</td>\r\n<td><span data-sort-value=\"Elonu, Chinemelu\"><span class=\"vcard\"><span class=\"fn\"><a title=\"Chinemelu Elonu\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinemelu_Elonu\">Chinemelu Elonu</a></span></span></span></td>\r\n<td style=\"text-align: center;\">F/C</td>\r\n<td><span class=\"flagicon\"><img class=\"thumbborder\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flag_of_Nigeria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Nigeria.svg.png\" Division I Basketball League\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_Division_I_Basketball_League\">Kuwait</a>)</td>\r\n<td>&nbsp;</td>\r\n<td style=\"text-align: center;\"><sup id=\"cite_ref-355\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-355\">[355]</a></sup></td>\r\n</tr>\r\n</tbody>\r\n<tfoot></tfoot>\r\n</table>\r\n<h3><span id=\"Draft_picks\" class=\"mw-headline\">Draft picks</span></h3>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"List of Los Angeles Lakers first and second round draft picks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Los_Angeles_Lakers_first_and_second_round_draft_picks\">List of Los Angeles Lakers first and second round draft picks</a></div>\r\n<p>The Lakers have had three <a title=\"List of first overall NBA draft picks\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_first_overall_NBA_draft_picks\">first overall picks</a> in their history: Elgin Baylor (selected in <a title=\"1958 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1958_NBA_draft\">1958</a>), Magic Johnson (selected in <a title=\"1979 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1979_NBA_draft\">1979</a>) and James Worthy (selected in <a title=\"1982 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_NBA_draft\">1982</a>).<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_Draft_History_356-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_Draft_History-356\">[356]</a></sup> The Lakers have also had six <a title=\"NBA draft lottery\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_draft_lottery\">lottery</a> picks in their history: Eddie Jones (selected tenth overall in <a title=\"1994 NBA draft\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1994_NBA_draft\">1994</a>), Andrew Bynum (selected tenth overall in 2005), Julius Randle (selected seventh overall in 2014), D'Angelo Russell (selected second overall in 2015), Brandon Ingram (selected second overall in 2016), and Lonzo Ball (selected second overall in 2017).<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_Draft_History_356-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_Draft_History-356\">[356]</a></sup> Other draft picks include Jerry West and Gail Goodrich in the 1960s, <a title=\"Michael Cooper\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Cooper\">Michael Cooper</a> and <a title=\"Norm Nixon\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norm_Nixon\">Norm Nixon</a> in the 1970s, <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"A.C. Green\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A.C._Green\">A.C. Green</a> and <a title=\"Vlade Divac\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vlade_Divac\">Vlade Divac</a> in the 1980s, <a title=\"Elden Campbell\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elden_Campbell\">Elden Campbell</a>, <a title=\"Nick Van Exel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nick_Van_Exel\">Nick Van Exel</a>, Derek Fisher, and <a title=\"Devean George\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Devean_George\">Devean George</a> in the 1990s, and <a title=\"Luke Walton\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luke_Walton\">Luke Walton</a>, <a title=\"Sasha Vujačić\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasha_Vuja%C4%8Di%C4%87\">Sasha Vujačić</a>, and <a title=\"Ronny Turiaf\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronny_Turiaf\">Ronny Turiaf</a> in the 2000s.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Lakers_Draft_History_356-2\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Lakers_Draft_History-356\">[356]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Head_coaches\" class=\"mw-headline\">Head coaches</span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\"><a class=\"image\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Phil_Jackson_3_cropped.jpg\"><img class=\"thumbimage\" src=\"https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Phil_Jackson_3_cropped.jpg/170px-Phil_Jackson_3_cropped.jpg\" srcset=\"//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Phil_Jackson_3_cropped.jpg/255px-Phil_Jackson_3_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Phil_Jackson_3_cropped.jpg/340px-Phil_Jackson_3_cropped.jpg 2x\" width=\"170\" height=\"240\" data-file-width=\"492\" data-file-height=\"695\"></a>\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">\r\n<div class=\"magnify\">&nbsp;</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"thumb tright\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbinner\" style=\"width: 172px;\">\r\n<div class=\"thumbcaption\">Former head coach Phil Jackson led the team to five championships.</div>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"List of Los Angeles Lakers head coaches\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Los_Angeles_Lakers_head_coaches\">List of Los Angeles Lakers head coaches</a></div>\r\n<p>There have been 22 head coaches for the Lakers franchise. <a title=\"John Kundla\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Kundla\">John Kundla</a> coached the team in Minneapolis when they won their first five <a title=\"NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBA_Finals\">BAA/NBA championships</a> from <a title=\"1949 BAA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949_BAA_Finals\">1949</a> to <a title=\"1954 NBA Finals\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1954_NBA_Finals\">1954</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-History_of_the_Lakers_#_10_47-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-History_of_the_Lakers_#_10-47\">[47]</a></sup> <a title=\"Pat Riley\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Riley\">Pat Riley</a> is second in franchise history in both regular season and playoff games coached and wins.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Riley_Stats_357-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Riley_Stats-357\">[357]</a></sup> Phil Jackson broke Riley's regular-season wins record in 2009, and he passed Riley's playoff wins and games coached records in 2010.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Riley_Stats_357-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Riley_Stats-357\">[357]</a></sup> Jackson, Riley, Kundla, and Bill Sharman have all been inducted into the Basketball Hall of Fame for their coaching careers. <a title=\"George Mikan\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Mikan\">George Mikan</a>, Jim Pollard, <a title=\"Jerry West\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerry_West\">Jerry West</a>, <a title=\"Pat Riley\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pat_Riley\">Pat Riley</a>, Magic Johnson, <a title=\"Kurt Rambis\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurt_Rambis\">Kurt Rambis</a>, <a title=\"Byron Scott\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byron_Scott\">Byron Scott</a> and <a title=\"Luke Walton\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luke_Walton\">Luke Walton</a> have all played and head-coached for the Lakers. Jackson, who had two stints as head coach, was coach from 2005 to 2011. In May 2011, <a title=\"Mike Brown (basketball, born 1970)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Brown_(basketball,_born_1970)\">Mike Brown</a> was named his replacement for the 2011&ndash;12 season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-358\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-358\">[358]</a></sup> Brown was fired<sup id=\"cite_ref-359\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-359\">[359]</a></sup> on November 9, 2012, after a 1&ndash;4 start. Assistant coach <a title=\"Bernie Bickerstaff\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bernie_Bickerstaff\">Bernie Bickerstaff</a> served as interim head coach for five games before the Lakers selected <a title=\"Mike D'Antoni\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_D%27Antoni\">Mike D'Antoni</a> as their new head coach. D'Antoni resigned at the end of the 2013&ndash;14 season. In July 2014, Byron Scott was hired as head coach.<sup id=\"cite_ref-360\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-360\">[360]</a></sup> After the 2015&ndash;16 season ended, Scott was fired. On April 29, 2016, former Lakers player <a title=\"Luke Walton\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luke_Walton\">Luke Walton</a> was named as Scott's replacement,<sup id=\"cite_ref-361\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-361\">[361]</a></sup> and served as head coach until the end of the 2018&ndash;19 season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-362\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-362\">[362]</a></sup> <a title=\"Frank Vogel\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Vogel\">Frank Vogel</a> was named his successor on a multiyear deal announced on May 13, 2019.<sup id=\"cite_ref-363\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-363\">[363]</a></sup> Vogel was fired following the conclusion of the 2021&ndash;22 season.<sup id=\"cite_ref-364\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-364\">[364]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Hall_of_Famers.2C_retired_and_honored_numbers\"></span><span id=\"Hall_of_Famers,_retired_and_honored_numbers\" class=\"mw-headline\">Hall of Famers, retired and honored numbers</span></h2>\r\n<p>The Lakers have 38 <a title=\"Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame\">Hall of Famers</a> (28 players, 5 head coaches, 1 assistant coach, and 4 contributors) who contributed to the organization.<sup id=\"cite_ref-365\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-365\">[365]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-366\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-366\">[366]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-367\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-367\">[367]</a></sup></p>\r\n<table class=\"wikitable\" style=\"text-align: center;\">\r\n<tbody>\r\n<tr>\r\n<th href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Point_guard\">G</a></td>\r\n<td>1949&ndash;1956</td>\r\n</tr>\r\n<tr>\r\n<td><strong>34</strong></td>\r\n<td><a title=\"Clyde Lovellette\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clyde_Lovellette\">Clyde Lovellette</a></td>\r\n<td><a title=\"Power forward (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_forward_(basketball)\">F</a>/<a title=\"Center (basketball)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Center_(basketball)\">C</a></td>\r\n<td>1953&ndash;1957</td>\r\n</tr>\r\n<tr>\r\n<td colspan=\"2\"><a title=\"John Kundla\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Kundla\">John Kundla</a></td>\r\n<td>Head coach</td>\r\n<td>1948&ndash;1957<br>1958&ndash;1959</td>\r\n</tr>\r\n</tbody>\r\n<tfoot></tfoot>\r\n</table>\r\n<h2><span id=\"Media\" class=\"mw-headline\">Media</span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"hatnote navigation-not-searchable\" role=\"note\">Main article: <a title=\"List of Los Angeles Lakers broadcasters\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Los_Angeles_Lakers_broadcasters\">List of Los Angeles Lakers broadcasters</a></div>\r\n<p>For 41 years, Chick Hearn was the team's broadcaster until his death in 2002. He broadcast 3,338 consecutive games between November 21, 1965, and December 16, 2001.<sup id=\"cite_ref-385\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-385\">[385]</a></sup> Hearn came up with West's \"Mr. Clutch\" nickname.<sup id=\"cite_ref-386\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-386\">[386]</a></sup> He was a part of the team's \"inner sanctum\" when Cooke was owner, and was consulted on basketball decisions.<sup id=\"cite_ref-387\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-387\">[387]</a></sup> <a title=\"Paul Sunderland\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Sunderland\">Paul Sunderland</a>, who had filled in for a couple of games while Hearn recuperated in the <a title=\"2001&ndash;02 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_NBA_season\">2001&ndash;02 season</a>, was named the permanent <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"Play-by-play\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Play-by-play\">play-by-play</a> announcer. <a title=\"Stu Lantz\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stu_Lantz\">Stu Lantz</a> was retained as the <a title=\"Color commentator\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Color_commentator\">color commentator</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-388\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-388\">[388]</a></sup> When Sunderland's contract expired in the summer of 2005, the team chose not to renew it.<sup id=\"cite_ref-389\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-389\">[389]</a></sup> Then, <a title=\"Joel Meyers\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joel_Meyers\">Joel Meyers</a> moved in alongside Lantz as the television announcer, with <a title=\"Spero Dedes\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spero_Dedes\">Spero Dedes</a> and former Laker player <a title=\"Mychal Thompson\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mychal_Thompson\">Mychal Thompson</a> on the radio.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_Broadcast_390-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_Broadcast-390\">[390]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>For the <a title=\"2011&ndash;12 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_NBA_season\">2011&ndash;12 season</a>, <a title=\"Bill Macdonald\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Macdonald\">Bill Macdonald</a> became the new television play-by-play announcer, joining Lantz who remained as the color analyst. Meanwhile, <a title=\"John Ireland (sportscaster)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Ireland_(sportscaster)\">John Ireland</a> joined Mychal Thompson to call the games on radio.<sup id=\"cite_ref-391\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-391\">[391]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>Beginning in the <a title=\"2009&ndash;10 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_NBA_season\">2009&ndash;10 season</a>, Lakers radio broadcasts were heard on <a title=\"KSPN (AM)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KSPN_(AM)\">KSPN</a> (Los Angeles <a title=\"ESPN Radio\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ESPN_Radio\">ESPN Radio</a> affiliate) in English and <a title=\"KWKW\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KWKW\">KWKW</a> in Spanish.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_Broadcast_390-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_Broadcast-390\">[390]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_Broadcast2_392-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_Broadcast2-392\">[392]</a></sup> <a class=\"mw-redirect\" title=\"KLAC (AM)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KLAC_(AM)\">KLAC</a> had the team's radio broadcast rights from the <a title=\"1976&ndash;77 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1976%E2%80%9377_NBA_season\">1976&ndash;77 season</a> until the <a title=\"2008&ndash;09 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_NBA_season\">2008&ndash;09 season</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Lakers_Broadcast2_392-1\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Lakers_Broadcast2-392\">[392]</a></sup><sup id=\"cite_ref-393\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-393\">[393]</a></sup> Until 2011, telecasts had been split between <a title=\"KCAL-TV\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KCAL-TV\">KCAL-TV</a> (road games) and Fox Sports West (home games), unless they are chosen for national broadcasts on <a title=\"ESPN on ABC\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ESPN_on_ABC\">ABC</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-schedule_394-0\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-schedule-394\">[394]</a></sup> KCAL had been the Lakers' over-the-air television broadcaster since 1977, dating back to when the station was the <a title=\"RKO General\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RKO_General\">RKO General</a>-owned KHJ-TV, the longest relationship between an NBA team and a television station. Prior to KHJ, Laker games were televised on <a title=\"KTLA\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KTLA\">KTLA</a>. The Lakers had been on Fox Sports West since 1985, dating to when it was the original Prime Ticket and owned by Buss.<sup id=\"cite_ref-395\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-395\">[395]</a></sup></p>\r\n<p>On February 14, 2011, <a title=\"Time Warner Cable\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_Warner_Cable\">Time Warner Cable</a> and the Lakers announced the formation of two new regional sports networks (one in English, one in Spanish) that would exclusively televise the team's games and related programming for 20 years starting with the <a title=\"2012&ndash;13 NBA season\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_NBA_season\">2012&ndash;13 season</a>.<sup id=\"cite_ref-396\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-396\">[396]</a></sup> The said networks were originally known as Time Warner Cable SportsNet, before it was renamed <a title=\"Spectrum SportsNet (Los Angeles)\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spectrum_SportsNet_(Los_Angeles)\">Spectrum SportsNet</a> in 2016 upon <a title=\"Charter Communications\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charter_Communications\">Charter Communications</a>' purchase of Time Warner Cable.<sup id=\"cite_ref-397\" class=\"reference\"><a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Lakers#cite_note-397\">[397]</a></sup></p>\r\n<h2><span id=\"References\" class=\"mw-headline\">References</span></h2>\r\n<div class=\"reflist\">\r\n<div class=\"mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns\">\r\n<ol class=\"references\">\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-1\"></li>\r\n</ol>\r\n</div>\r\n</div>\r\n<ul>\r\n<li id=\"cite_note-1\"><span class=\"reference-text\"><cite class=\"citation web cs1\"><a class=\"external text\" href=\"https://www.nba.com/lakers/history/seasonbyseason\" rel=\"nofollow\">\"Lakers Season-by-Season Records\"</a>. <em>Lakers.com</em>.
